>   MUST receive no target event across a full bounded window.** They are NOT symmetric; an OFF phase can never be

>   then reject B.** A poll-time freshness stamp is REFUTED — re-reading cached state refreshes the stamp with no

> **★ MY DEAD CONJECTURE FOUND A LIVE DEFECT IN CORE'S CRATE — and core's ruling then INVERTED my own follow-up task, which I REPLACED rather than annotated (core `5e6384e`, RX-side only, NO wire bytes, cannot invalidate `d4c65886`).** core traced WHY `r2-dataplane:943` hardcodes `false` and found the opposite of what my conjecture implied: **`R2-WIRE.md:178` — "M = 1 = ORIGINATED BY a reduced-capability companion MCU" — is a claim about `originator` (route_stack[0]), NOT about `immediate_source` (the peer we heard from). They coincide ONLY on a single-hop frame.** `sync_host.rs:263` was reading the bit straight into a neighbour entry keyed on `immediate_source` ⇒ **a companion MCU originates, a full-stack RELAY forwards, we observe the RELAY, mark the RELAY `mcu_only`, `is_viable=false`, and the relay drops out of every flood plan — and it STICKS (`neighbour.rs:349-353` re-clears only on an observation carrying `mcu_origin=false`). A capable relay leaves the route fabric as a REWARD for carrying a companion's frames.** Fixed as `header.flags.mcu_origin && originator == immediate_source`, failing open deliberately: wrongly believing a neighbour relays costs one dropped frame plus a confidence penalty; wrongly believing it does NOT removes it from the fabric until something re-clears the bit. ✎ **THIS REFUTES MY OWN TASK #86, whose premise was "dfr1195 hardcodes `false` on RX ⇒ ignores a real signal ⇒ should propagate" — that was exactly the fix direction core was about to take and then didn't. dfr1195's hardcoded `false` at `:1428`/`:1453`/`:1945` is CORRECT for multi-hop. #86 rewritten (not annotated) to the NARROW surviving gap: on a SINGLE-HOP frame, where `originator == immediate_source` and the bit IS valid, we still discard it, so we never learn a genuine companion MCU is tx-only. Low priority, no symptom.** **SCOPING FACT recorded so nobody sizes it as trivial: the dfr1195 obs site has `immediate_source` ONLY (`main.rs:1937` `Observation { hive_id: sender_hive, .. }`); `route_stack[0]` is NOT in scope, so core's guard is a plumbing change here, and when patched it MUST match core's shape rather than a hive-invented variant.** ⚠ **core's fix is a SECOND #63 candidate — a better one than the M bit — but ONLY on boards that run `sync_host`. dfr1195 does NOT (Path C, proven), so it is not mine. OPEN AND UNOWNED: which boards run `sync_host`? Neither core nor I know; that MUST be answered by whoever owns those platforms before anyone re-tests #63 against `5e6384e`.** ~core also accepted Path C and stated the distinction I would have skipped: its enumeration was "complete FOR CORE, wrong FOR THE FLEET" (grep `Observation {` across core's `platforms/`+`tools/` = ZERO). ~It promoted the masking insight as a general shape: **two independent defects in OPPOSITE directions where one suppresses the other's symptom — which is why "no symptom" is not evidence of "no defect", same family as an unfired gate.**
> **✖ MY M-BIT/#63 CONJECTURE IS DEAD — killed by my own trace, via a THIRD RX path core did not enumerate. THE CONFORMANCE DEFECT SURVIVES AND IS OWED.** core answered my falsifier by naming two core-side paths (Path A `r2-dataplane/src/lib.rs:943` hardcodes `mcu_origin: false` ⇒ M never propagates; Path B `r2-hive-core/src/sync_host.rs:263` propagates `header.flags.mcu_origin` ⇒ mechanism holds) and asked which loop dfr1195 runs. **ANSWER: NEITHER. dfr1195 runs no `sync_host` (grep: 2 COMMENT hits at main.rs:48/:6607, ZERO calls) and does not take neighbour obs from r2-dataplane — it CONSTRUCTS ITS OWN `Observation`s in platform code at THREE sites and HARDCODES the bit at every one: `:1422`→`:1428 mcu_origin: false`, `:1447`→`:1453 false`, `:1937`→`:1945 false`. `header.flags.mcu_origin` is NEVER READ on this board** ⇒ the received M bit cannot reach `mcu_only`, cannot reach `is_viable`, and core's sticky-clear rule (`neighbour.rs:349-353`) never even gets a chance to fire. **⇒ #63 mesh-wide nbrs=0 is NOT M-bit caused on dfr1195. PATH C exists — platform-local Observation construction — and core's two-path model is incomplete; any platform doing this is immune to the M bit in BOTH directions regardless of which core loop it links.** ★ **THE TWO DEFECTS MASK EACH OTHER, which is why neither surfaced: RX hardcodes `false` (we IGNORE a real signal, treating even a genuine companion MCU as relay-viable) while TX emits `true` (we SEND a false signal, advertising tx-only while relaying). Opposite directions — and the RX bug is precisely what stops the TX bug producing the symptom that would have exposed it. Two independent defects, NOT one bug that cancels.** ⇒ **core's ruling stands unweakened and I am not letting the dead conjecture argue it away: M=1 at a relaying dfr1195 is a FALSE SELF-CLAIM on the wire (R2-WIRE §4.2.1 v0.45), a conformance defect independent of #63. Mine to patch, core's to rule — it ruled M MUST be 0 at the six TX sites.** ⚠ **SEQUENCING HELD AND ESCALATED, NOT DECIDED ALONE: the staged artifact `d4c65886…` is PINNED (manifest `398cf31`) awaiting a Roy-gated flash, and patching main.rs moves the bytes on six emit paths. I MUST NOT silently invalidate a staged artifact mid-flight — that is exactly the stale-artefact-vs-moved-tree divergence composer caught here once. Options put to supervisor: (A) patch AFTER the bench, my recommendation — the defect is long-standing, not a live safety risk, and no bench item measures the M bit; (B) patch now + rebuild + new sha + re-offer to Roy; (C) patch without rebuilding — REJECTED outright. NOTHING PATCHED pending the ruling.** ✎ **SECOND defect flagged and UNSCOPED: the RX hardcoding is its own patch; I have not sized it and am not claiming it.**

NOTHING PATCHED (core owns the wire rule and made the per-board call for esp32-s3; this is its ruling to make).** core's discipline is: the M bit is a PER-BOARD ROLE CLAIM, trace whether relay is IMPLEMENTED, never sweep by pattern — it verified esp32-s3's M=1 as CORRECT because relay there is an unimplemented M4 milestone. **Doing the same trace on dfr1195 inverts the answer: SIX TX sites emit `Flags { mcu_origin: true, .. }` (main.rs:1498, :1703, :1768, :1841, :2395, :6110) while `lora_route_task`/`relay_append`/`note_forwarded` appear 20× in that same file ⇒ relay IS implemented ⇒ the tx-only claim is FALSE.** ★ **Our own code states the consequence, and it is FUNCTIONAL not cosmetic — main.rs:1943 verbatim: "FULL ESP32 node, NOT mcu_only — must be relay-viable (core: `mcu_origin:true` → `is_viable=false` → `build_flood_plan` finds 0 neighbours → `Drop(NoViableNeighbour)`)". I have NOT traced that path — do not act on this until someone does.** ✎ **METHOD CORRECTION owed and reported: my first pass concluded "all `mcu_origin` false" from a `head -20` listing — a truncated pipe read as a clean result. Real counts are 25 true-sites in dfr1195-fw and 11 in rak4630-fw. > **⚔ GRUNT 0.1 REFUTATION (my assigned lens: reality check — encode a REAL message and report what breaks). VERDICTS: §3 KILLED · §4 KILLED · §6 WOUNDED (not for the stated reason) · §8 SURVIVED-my-axis. Roy-authored draft; NOT ratified; attack-before-hardening was the instruction.** All numbers measured with the fleet's own `tools/comms-fitness.py` (o200k_base) on messages I actually sent today — and supervisor's polarity count-fix is live in it, which is what produced finding 1. ★ **FINDING 1 — §3+§4 CANNOT ENCODE A NEGATIVE OBLIGATION. That is a GRAMMAR failure, not a budget one, and it kills both sections for safety traffic.** §3's closed set is `ASK | TELL | DO | DONE | FAIL | NEED | GOT | UPD` — **eight performatives, not one expressing PROHIBITION** (no DENY, no HOLD, no MUST-NOT form); and §4's "CONTENT WORDS ONLY" means "MUST NOT" does not survive the register. **MEASURED on my real refutation of the scorer: v2 as sent = 535 tok, 8/8 facts. GRUNT under the 128 cap = 26 tok, 0/8 facts, REJECT. GRUNT with FULL evidence = 106 tok — INSIDE the cap — 6/8 facts, STILL REJECT, losing `MUST NOT` and `dcee2a9`, polarity reporting "7 negative obligations before, 0 after".** ⇒ **the budget was never the binding constraint; the grammar is. Supervisor's finding 4 said a budget with no capability gate becomes PRESSURE to drop a MUST NOT — it is worse: there is NO SLOT to drop it from.** ★ **FINDING 2 — GRUNT would force me to MIS-ENCODE today's live state as its OPPOSITE.** "Item 2 HELD / NO INSTRUMENT — never pass, never fail" has no performative: `TELL` asserts a fact, but a HOLD is a prohibition on judging, and the nearest fit is `FAIL item2 ; cause no-instrument` — **which says the observer FAILED. It did not; it has never been judged. A takeover reads FAIL, concludes the firmware is broken, and "fixes" working code — the exact false-red class this whole day was spent eliminating.** ★ **FINDING 3 — §4 "NO META" DIRECTLY CONTRADICTS COMMS.md §2, and both are Roy-authored.** §4 forbids restating/editorializing; COMMS.md §2 requires a refutation keep its evidence chain and says refutation reasoning MUST NOT be compressed. **The 535→106 gap is almost entirely `^` scope/mechanism lines — §4 calls them meta, COMMS.md calls them the evidence. One MUST yield in text, or every refuter guesses differently.** ~**§6 WOUNDED:** my five messages that turn measured 354/454/486/523/555 tok (mean 474), all over the 128 hard cap, none padding; §6 says over-budget MUST go to the blackboard, but §5 needs §9's ETS/`:pg`/GenServer runtime that does not exist ⇒ **today the only conformant way to obey §6 is TO DELETE EVIDENCE.** ~§8 survived my axis (cache invalidation is circuits' lens). ~§2/§5/§7 NOT attacked by me — **my silence there is not a pass.** **Open question routed to Roy, needs a ruling not an opinion: is GRUNT meant to carry SAFETY traffic at all, or only task/status coordination with refutations staying in v2? If the latter, findings 1-3 shrink to a §0 scope note; if the former, §3 needs a new performative class.**

One cache lifetime is implementation/config-specific; it MAY reproduce the risk, it MUST NOT derive a wait bound. Stronger point handed over: an EVENT-stamped design does not NEED a timeout at all — freshness is proven by the event's own arrival, so deriving a window from a measurement would re-import the polling model it is removing. Also re-flagged that the measurement REQUIRES a synthetic R2-shaped advertiser (`parse_r2_mfr` ignores everything else).** composer takes that item under the constraint; I am not claiming it.

> **✅ ANSWERED core's open question — THE WORKSPACE EXCLUSION IS NOT INERTIA, so its new grep gate is the CORRECT PERMANENT FIX rather than a stopgap.** `Cargo.toml:38-44` carries the reason inline on every entry: `platforms/esp32` is a **different target triple** (`xtensa-esp32s3-espidf`, `:39`), and likewise dfr1195 (`xtensa-esp32s3-none-elf`), nrf54-lr2021 (`thumbv8m.main-none-eabi`), rak4630 (`thumbv7em-none-eabihf`), and rak4630-bootloader (a DIFFERENT embassy than the app). A cargo workspace shares one resolver and feature unification, so a no_std MCU triple CANNOT join a std host workspace — checking from the root yields a false std/`serde_core` flood that reads as a firmware break ([[mcu-cargo-check-from-package-dir]]). ⇒ **Joining the workspace does NOT beat the grep gate; the exclusion is load-bearing and permanent.** ★ **GENERALISED back to core: any check that must see excluded platforms MUST be SOURCE-level (raw `git grep` over tracked files), never cargo-level — cargo tooling is STRUCTURALLY blind here, not merely unconfigured. That is precisely why `platforms/unoq` hid until the grep ran, and core's gate caught that missed site on its FIRST run — a positive control firing.** This came from my own "fixing the call site does not fix the class; exclusion IS the class" point, which core acted on.
> **📄 SCOPE RULING (Roy via supervisor, 2026-07-19) — THE COMPRESSION IS FOR INTER-AI COMMS ONLY; ALL DOCUMENTATION STAYS PROSE and deliberately MORE verbose than agent-to-agent traffic.** That covers this file, handoff records, `AGENTS.md`, READMEs, **spec bodies** (a spec reader IS a human — specs MUST NOT compress §12.2 prose while fixing it), code comments, and commit messages. **RFC 2119 keywords STILL apply to documentation — they ADD precision. The DENSE WIRE FORMAT does NOT.** Rationale worth keeping: optimising a token budget against a human reader is a FALSE ECONOMY — the cost never lands in the budget, it lands later as a misunderstanding, **and the fitness function CANNOT measure it because it only scores agent-to-agent encodings.** ✎ **This lands on me: my earlier `AGENTS.md` line said compression applies "to agent-to-agent fleet messages, not only human-facing output", which predates the ruling and reads as licensing compressed docs. > **✅ SUPERVISOR FIXED MY `comms-fitness.py` FINDING (`claude-fleet dcee2a9`) — I RE-RAN IT RATHER THAN INHERITING IT, AND FOUND A RESIDUAL HOLE.** The fix holds on 6 probes, 3 of which I invented beyond my original report: MUST NOT→MUST REJECTs (polarity is flagged even when the caller declared ONLY "MUST" — the independent check earns its keep exactly there), `recipe.rs:1749`/`17490` REJECTs, SHOULD NOT→SHOULD REJECTs, an honest MUST NOT ADOPTs, a declared-MUST-NOT inversion REJECTs, and supervisor's own `:`-exclusion over-correction is genuinely closed (`repo@abc1234:src/main.rs:42` survives as one fact). ★ **RESIDUAL — COUNT-BLINDNESS: polarity is PRESENCE-based while obligation loss is COUNT-based.** `"=MUST NOT flash and MUST NOT push @d4c65886"` → `"=MUST NOT flash @d4c65886"` scores `facts_lost []`, verdict **ADOPT** — **one of TWO MUST NOT obligations silently dropped, because "MUST NOT" is still present.** **This is the ORIGINAL defect one level in: declared as presence, matched as presence, never COUNTED — the fix moved it from substring-blind to count-blind.** Live, not theoretical: fleet messages routinely carry several MUSTs (mine that turn carried four). ⇒ the polarity check SHOULD compare per-keyword OCCURRENCE COUNTS before-vs-after, not membership. ~Precision cost flagged as a CHOICE not an accident: MUST NOT→SHALL NOT REJECTs, which is a legitimate RFC 2119 synonym; defensible (keyword churn is bad) but supervisor's own crying-wolf warning applies — a scorer that rejects legal rewrites gets routed around.
> **⛔ DO NOT START — §12.2 WiFi-provisioning is being RE-SPECCED (supervisor, Roy-authorized this turn). specs authors; core owns the wire/event side; hive builds the ESP platform that implements the currently-unguarded path. WAIT FOR FROZEN TEXT.** **The current ESP behaviour is CONFORMANT to canon as written ⇒ it is NOT a hive defect and MUST NOT be "fixed" against the old text.** I supplied specs implementer ground truth only (caller-traced, not symbol-absence): `platforms/esp32/src/wifi_prov.rs` has ZERO claim/auth/verify/tg_hash/hmac/sign symbols; `decode_wifi_config` has ONE caller (`main.rs:638`), `save_credentials` ONE (`:642`), `clear_credentials` ONE (`:681`); the ONLY predicate on the write path is `msg.event_hash == wifi_config_hash` (`:636`), and **`from_addr` IS available and LOGGED (`:637`) but never CHECKED — an enforcement POINT exists, nothing enforces at it.** `wifi_clear` (`:677-681`) has **no gate whatsoever**, so specs' "owner auth OR physical reset" is net-new enforcement rather than a tightening. ★ **Emittability check handed back on specs' own draft: there is NO claim-state variable anywhere in the ESP platform — not unset, ABSENT — so a clause phrased "accept `wifi_config` only while UNCLAIMED" would have NO PRODUCER here and would be phantom gate #6. Either name where claim-state is stored and what sets it, or mark it ENFORCEMENT OWED + INERT.** A sender-identity clause, by contrast, already has its enforcement point in hand.

> **⚠ android RETRACTED its 30 s evidence-TTL claim to me (2026-07-19) and I had ALREADY moved my risk posture on it — manifest now states the TTL MUST NOT be cited as an adv+scan coexistence safety net.** It bounds a CLEAN STOP only (carrier stops, TTL expires, phone resumes ~5 s). It does NOT bound a STUCK carrier: sightings are unauthenticated BY DESIGN (`core-ffi/src/beacon.rs:350` — "No HMAC — a sighting is unauthenticated discovery, not a member Event"), there is no replay/counter/nonce in `core-ffi/src/control.rs`, and `R2UsbDriver.kt:454` stamps receipt time on EVERY valid sighting ⇒ one cached observation re-emitted under 30 s refreshes the evidence forever and holds the phone deaf indefinitely **with no attacker involved**. The gate proves a REPORT ARRIVED, not that ACQUISITION HAPPENED. **Nothing unsafe today:** `feat/carrier-ble-handoff` is HELD/unmerged, `carrierBleProven` absent from `master`, deployed APK has NO handoff ⇒ the phone's BLE cannot stand down at first light ⇒ bench unaffected, observer image needs no change. **★ Checked my own file with a POSITIVE CONTROL before claiming the clean state: `grep -i ttl` = 0 hits, and the same grep fires 6× on `d4c65886`/`bearer` and 2× on `handoff` ⇒ the null is from absence, not a broken instrument ([[never-conclude-from-a-null]]).** Counter-conjecture sent back to android on its paused fix: a periodic independent phone-scan override bounds suppression by TIME, but the poisoning is by CONTENT — consecutive-identical observation bytes are a stronger stuck-detector than a timer and cost no extra radio; asked whether core-ffi retains the raw AD post-parse to allow byte-equality.
> **✖ MY duplicate-detection counter-conjecture KILLED by android (2026-07-19) — and its premise is TRUE IN MY OWN TREE, which is where I should have checked before proposing it.** I argued consecutive-identical observation bytes beat a timer as a stuck-carrier detector. android refuted on merits AND answered the FFI question: the raw AD does NOT survive to Kotlin (`FfiSighting` = parsed fields only, `uniffi/r2_core_ffi.kt:4644-4680`), so byte-equality would need an FFI change — but the idea fails before that cost. **VERIFIED AT MY SOURCE, stronger than android's parsed-field argument: `anti_collision: 0` is HARDCODED (main.rs:3545), `LegacyBeacon` is built ONCE outside the advertise loop (main.rs:3535), and `let epoch: u64 = 0;` (main.rs:3533, comment: "epoch=0 placeholder until the shared coarse-time base wires in") ⇒ every AD byte from a stationary board is LITERALLY IDENTICAL every time.** So identical-content is the HEALTHY NORM at epoch 0 and my detector flags every healthy stationary device — false positive on the common case. The only varying field is `rssi`, which is carrier-MEASURED not in the AD, so a stuck carrier replays cached rssi too and any firmware can jitter one byte: weak and spoofable. **Time-bounded max-off watchdog CONCEDED as primary — it bounds suppression regardless of report CONTENT, the property that survives an adversary CHOOSING the content (same shape as our no-simulated-red bar).** ✎ **COUNTER-FINDING handed back on android's "MAY revisit post-rotation" variant: it would false-positive on THIS firmware permanently — `current_beacon_epoch()` (main.rs:4807) returns literal `0`, and `LORA_BEACON_T_ROTATE_S = 3600` (main.rs:4768) is referenced only by `let _ =` to silence dead-code ⇒ dfr1195 NEVER rotates rbid on either bearer, so "unchanged rbid across a T_rotate boundary is diagnostic" would fire continuously against a correctly-working board. The detector's precondition is a firmware capability that does not exist yet.** Also queried: android cites BLE `T_rotate` = 900 s, my LoRa constant is 3600 s (§8.1.3) — if the bearers genuinely differ that's fine, but one of us may hold a stale number and it should settle before either side builds on it.
> **🚨 THE FLEET'S NEW ADOPTION GATE BLESSES A SAFETY INVERSION — `comms-fitness.py` WOUNDED, reported to supervisor (claude-fleet is ITS repo; I did NOT edit it).** Roy's PROTOCOL-EVOLVES directive makes fitness = fewer tokens AND capability maintained, measured by `tools/comms-fitness.py`, with capability as a GATE not a term. **I applied today's own rule before trusting it: caller-grepped (all 5 fns wired) and RAN it (`.venv/bin/python3`, "ALL CONTROLS FIRED"). The 3 shipped negative controls are REAL — they simply do not RANGE OVER this class.** ★ **ROOT CAUSE (`:40`): `lost = [f for f in facts if f and f not in after]` — facts are DECLARED as tokens but MATCHED as UNANCHORED SUBSTRINGS.** **PROBE A, reproducible, verbatim output: before `"=MUST NOT flash board B without the Roy gate @d4c65886"` → after `"=MUST flash B @d4c65886"`, facts `["MUST","d4c65886"]` ⇒ `facts_kept 2`, `facts_lost []`, `delta -6`, `pct -37.5`, verdict **`ADOPT`**. "MUST" IS A SUBSTRING OF "MUST NOT", so the gate scores a REVERSED SAFETY DIRECTIVE as capability-preserved and RECOMMENDS it — the single most dangerous compression available in this fleet.** PROBE B: fact `recipe.rs:1749` vs after `@recipe.rs:17490` ⇒ `facts_kept 1`, `ADOPT` — a WRONG `file:line` scores as kept. ⇒ **MUST NOT treat `facts_kept` as capability-preserved until matching is BOUNDARY-ANCHORED; RFC 2119 negatives MUST be a CLOSED VOCABULARY matched LONGEST-FIRST (MUST NOT / SHALL NOT / SHOULD NOT are DISTINCT facts, never substrings of MUST / SHALL / SHOULD); and the selftest MUST gain BOTH as negative controls, else the fix is unverifiable in the direction that matters.** ★★ **Supervisor said a PROSE fitness function would have been phantom gate #6. This one is NOT phantom — it emits, and its controls fire. The defect is narrower and nastier: ITS PREDICATE CANNOT SEE THE FAILURE IT EXISTS TO CATCH. Same family as my console that does not print, my MAC probe already on the allowlist, and my scanner that cannot parse the advertiser — the fourth instance today, and the first one I caught in someone ELSE's instrument before it was used on me.**
> **⚠ codex F1-F3 ON MY OWN FRESHNESS WRITE-UP — ALL THREE CONFIRMED, landed dfr1195-fw `eac59d4` (docs-only, sha `d4c65886…` unchanged). TWO ARE ERRORS I MADE WHILE RECORDING SOMEONE ELSE'S CATCH.** **F1 — TOOL-LOCAL STALENESS IS A SECOND, INDEPENDENT DEFECT: fixing BlueZ freshness does NOT close it.** `found = {}` is initialised once (`:181`), only ever written (`:202`), never expired or cleared, and `--expect` evaluates `any(found)` (`:250-253`) ⇒ **one RBID observed at ANY point stays PASS for the WHOLE PROCESS even with a perfectly fresh BlueZ layer underneath.** Fix must expire by fresh-event time OR run each phase as an isolated cache-purged process. **F2 — MY OVER-CLAIM: I asserted "BlueZ retains the device object and its `manufacturer_data` after the advertiser stops" as FACT, then called persistence UNMEASURED in the same breath.** Inconsistent, and the assertion went past its evidence: `TEST-RIG.md:246-258` documents stale **PRE-advertiser** caching, **which is NOT evidence of POST-STOP retention.** The manifest now claims ONLY that an OFF-phase reading CAN be cached and is therefore not proof of air; **no stop-retention behaviour is asserted.** **F3 — MY MEASUREMENT PROPOSAL WAS WRONG TWICE, do not run it as written:** (a) `parse_r2_mfr` (`:109-119`) accepts only R2-shaped manufacturer data (`COMPANY_AS_EMITTED`, or `COMPANY_DOCUMENTED` with `p[0] == MAGIC`) ⇒ **an arbitrary BLE device NEVER ENTERS `found`**, so my "advertise from anything" test would have measured NOTHING and returned a clean null — **a null from an instrument that cannot see the phenomenon, which is the exact defect I have now made three times today**; a synthetic R2-shaped advertiser is REQUIRED. (b) Even run correctly, **one observed cache lifetime is implementation/config-specific and MUST NOT become an OFF-wait timeout — it can REPRODUCE the risk, it cannot SIZE the acceptance.** ⇒ **Acceptance MUST rest on an explicit fresh EVENT or a verified purge per isolated phase, NEVER on a wait bound.**

> **📡 STANDING (Roy 2026-07-19) — CAVEMAN COMPRESSION APPLIES AGENT-TO-AGENT, not just agent-to-human.** Fleet token spend is dominated by per-turn context; inter-agent messages are a large share. Unsure? Write it long; a re-ask costs more than the tokens saved. [[compress-agent-to-agent-comms]]

> **📏 STANDING (Roy 2026-07-19, relayed by supervisor) — AGENT-TO-AGENT COMMS MUST USE RFC 2119 NORMATIVE LANGUAGE.** Appended to `AGENTS.md` V2 OVERRIDE block, commit `9f883a0` on main (pure append: `git diff --numstat` = 27 added / 0 removed; 8 top-level sections before and after; `ci/public-hygiene.sh` OK). **RFC 8174 is the load-bearing half: ONLY UPPERCASE IS NORMATIVE** — lowercase "must" is prose and binds nobody, so an instruction without a capitalised keyword is INFORMATIONAL and the recipient MUST say so rather than obeying it. This COMPOSES with the compression rule instead of fighting it: RFC 2119 REPLACES hedged prose ("it would be good if this were verified before freeze" → "This MUST be verified before freeze") = shorter AND unambiguous. SHOULD = MAY deviate WITH a stated reason; MUST = MAY NOT deviate, and on inability the lane MUST STOP and report rather than work around. Do NOT capitalise for emphasis (a keyword is a contract, not a shout). RELAYED requirements MUST name the source lane so obligation and provenance stay separable.
> **📏 RULING (supervisor, fleet-wide 2026-07-19) — MEMORY.md COMPRESSION IS OFF; the discriminator is LINK DENSITY.** High link-or-reference density ⇒ index-like ⇒ DO NOT COMPRESS; prose with few refs is the only safe target. **WHY it matters more than the token count: my caveman-compress defect was LOUD on RESUME.md (headings 17→0, ~1000 inline spans, it aborted and wrote nothing) — on an INDEX the same defect is SILENT, the file still reads fine while the `[[links]]` stop resolving. Damage you cannot see is worse than damage that aborts.** Archival split does not rescue an index either (no dated tail to move). **Final fleet position on the three files: `MEMORY.md` never compress/split · `RESUME.md` manual archival split ONLY (move verbatim, diff the tail byte-identical) · `AGENTS.md` append-only, never rewrite.** hive `memory/MEMORY.md` = 19942 B, never compressed, unchanged. ✎ **Correction I sent back (source lane = hive):** the ruling quotes specs' measurement (58 links / 6 headings / 4 backtick spans in 9758 B) as fleet-wide ground; that is SPECS' file — hive's is ~2× the size and I have not measured its link density. The conclusion holds for hive on the STRUCTURAL argument, but a per-lane number MUST NOT be relayed as a fleet measurement. ✎ Supervisor also closed its own error: it had told the fleet RESUME.md was the per-turn token win; composer refuted it and hive+specs confirmed in their own trees — three lanes, no repo CLAUDE.md ⇒ **RESUME.md is takeover-read cost only. GREP THE LOADER, never assume a file auto-loads.** The RESUME splits still stand on verified ground: both specs and composer found STALE takeover headers naming merged/abandoned branches, and composer's named a branch that STILL EXISTS ⇒ a takeover would have checked it out successfully and worked dead code with no error. **A stale pointer that RESOLVES is worse than one that errors.**

> **🔒 CUSTODY / NO-LITERALS RULE (supervisor fleet-wide ruling 2026-07-17 — I VIOLATED this; see the incident note below).**
> Real attribution (hive_id / origin / tg_hash / hk) and any vector DERIVED from a real persona are SECRETS and MUST NOT appear as
> literals in ANY tracked artifact — code, comments, examples, test fixtures, docs, RESUME prose, or COMMIT MESSAGES. Documenting a
> secret IS publishing it. **The public-hygiene gate does NOT protect this class** (it matches 12-hex MAC shapes; an 8-hex hive_id /
> tg_hash sails straight through — a green gate is NOT a leak-check). Committed content stays SYNTHETIC-BY-DEFAULT; real values are
> read AT RUNTIME from gitignored custody (`~/.r2-dev-trial/*.bin`, mode 600) or env — the hive-live-view.mjs pattern. "Lock to
> PROVISIONED" ALWAYS means at RUNTIME, never "commit the values". Regenerate vectors locally via the scratchpad vecgen harness
> (parses the custody persona with r2-trust + the real r2-wire codec); hand them to peers over fleet, never via a tracked file.

> **🛑 THREE MORE HOLES — MY `cfc6ba2` BOUND IS INSUFFICIENT AND CORE'S CORRECTION IS ALSO WRONG-LAYER (2026-07-17). NOTHING FLASHED.**
> **⚠ FALSIFIER RUN (not reasoned): THREE WINDOWS, ONE GATE.** **VERIFIED:** `main.rs:474` `let mut buf = [0u8; 512]` (**FIELD** reads only **512 B**) · `persona_from_bytes(BAKED_PERSONA)` whole slice (**BAKED**, unbounded) · `PERSONA_LEN = 0x2000` (**8192**). **A persona with a 400-byte key-3 — aggregate ends at byte 705 — is ADMITTED by my gate (705 ≤ 8192) while the FIELD runtime's 512-byte read parses to `None` ⇒ HARD-STOP. A GREEN BUILD THAT BRICKS.** Same class as the duplicate-key divergence.
> **★★ CORE'S CORRECTION ("the PRODUCER owns capacity") FAILS ITS OWN DE-DUP RULING** — it puts a bound in `build.rs` **AND** `build-field-image.sh` = **two implementations of a safety check** = the divergence that started this thread. **AND the 512 IS NOT SHARED GEOMETRY**: it is a bare literal at `main.rs:474`, **ZERO hits in rak-geometry** ⇒ "derived from shared geometry" names a const that **does not exist**, so implementing it would hardcode a **second 512 free to drift**. Same defect, new number. **Core's own diagnosis of itself is right and applies twice: it collapsed a GEOMETRY fact into a SEMANTIC one, first by deleting my capacity check on a CLASS ruling, then by restoring it into the WRONG LAYER.**
> **★★★ MY COUNTER-PROPOSAL — TESTED, FIRES BOTH WAYS, NO HAND-ROLLED WALKER: DO NOT COMPUTE THE AGGREGATE END — *SIMULATE THE CONSUMER*.** Hand **the runtime's own parser** exactly the bytes **the runtime will see**: `parse_persona(&persona[..len.min(FIELD_READ_WINDOW)])`. **MEASURED:** 705 B → **REJECT** (matches the runtime exactly) · real 336 B → **accept** (non-vacuity). **That is the acceptance-set rule taken to its conclusion: the gate doesn't MODEL the consumer, it RUNS the consumer's predicate over the consumer's window.** **PROPOSED SHAPE (core's to rule/falsify): ONE semantic core, TWO ENTRY POINTS, one per PRODUCER** — `validate_for_baked` (semantics, whole slice) · `validate_for_field_swd` (`file_len ≤ PERSONA_LEN` **protects ACTIVE from the write overrun** AND semantics **over the 512-window** **protects the field runtime from a truncated parse**). **NOT a target PARAMETER** — a param can be passed wrong and the dangerous direction (Baked-target on a field build) **fails OPEN**; two entry points make the wrong target **unrepresentable**. **PREREQ: `FIELD_READ_WINDOW` must become a rak-geometry const consumed by `main.rs:474`, or I build the very divergence I am closing.** KATs owed: **511/512/513 AND 8191/8192/8193**, both measures.
> **★ (1) ROLE/GUEST — core says my `0x01..0x04` scope ADMITS GUEST** (R2-TRUST §8.4: guest = role `0x04`, **4-hour** lifetime, scoped `DEK_guest`, **never** group DEK/HK — but the KS1 persona **always** carries full DEK+HK and the RAK builds GroupHmac straight from HK at `main.rs:778-789`, never reading role or window) ⇒ **an anchored, correctly-signed GUEST cert is elevated to a full accepted-HK participant indefinitely. An AUTHORIZATION/TYPE mismatch no signature path can catch.** **NOT LANDED — I have not read §8.4 myself and will not take it on say-so given 3-of-4.** Core's own form is the right fix: ***a Guest persona that can hold HK AT ALL is the bug; rejecting it at a gate is the patch — the TYPE, not the CHECK.*** Patch (reject `0x04`+`0x05`) after I read it.
> **★ (3) OPEN ATTACK, NOT CLOSED BY ANYTHING DESIGNED — TG-ONLY ADMISSION CLONES IDENTITIES.** Even with #76 landed, the gate accepts **ANY** valid member persona of the anchored TG ⇒ **swap D4's or the XIAO's persona onto the RAK and it clones a certified identity and passes.** **Worse for us specifically: `d4-persona.bin`, `rak-persona.bin` AND `xiao-persona.bin` ALL carry TG `730c29e7` — the clone material is in the same custody directory.** **#76 proves SELF-CONSISTENT MEMBERSHIP, not THIS-BOARD.** Canon R2-PROVISION §4.1 wants a unique stable device identity; Path B binds an expected fingerprint for exactly this. > **🛑✅ ONE GATE, TWO PRODUCERS — THE FIELD RECIPE WAS UNGATED AND MY OWN KNOWN-BAD ARTIFACT PASSED IT. FIXED `e3579ce` (2026-07-17). NO-FLASH held; nothing flashed.**

> **DOUBLE CONSEQUENCE:** **(1)** it **bypasses the #72 hard-stop** — that lives in the BAKED path; the field build reads `0x22000` and the app's parser accepts an empty cert ⇒ `Some` ⇒ **radio configured. The fail-open-into-radiation I closed was still open on the other road.** **(2)** it **BECOMES THE OTA SIGNING ROOT** (bootloader reads a strict key5 from `0x22000` as its update anchor). **One artifact: a radiating relay AND a trusted update path.**
> **★★★ THE SHAPE — THE NIGHT'S DISEASE ONE LEVEL UP: *WE HARDENED THE ROAD THAT WAS ALREADY SAFER.*** core asked *"which value does the CONSUMER read"* and **stopped one noun short**; I asked *"which CONSUMER"* properly and found the bootloader uncovered; **NOBODY ASKED WHICH PRODUCER WRITES.** **Three lanes, three passes, and the write side went unexamined until core-codex looked.** ⇒ **ask the question on BOTH sides of the value: which consumer READS it, and WHICH PRODUCER WRITES IT.**
> **FIX:** `r2-persona-gate` now ships a **CLI**; `build-field-image.sh` **CALLS it and HARD-FAILS**. **The two shell predicates are DELETED ON PURPOSE** — re-adding them would be a **THIRD acceptance set**, the same divergence one layer down. Post-flash **readback/digest-match** added to the emitted recipe. **CONTROLS (exit measured UNPIPED):** known-BAD → **exit 1 + ZERO recipe lines**; known-GOOD → exit 0, proceeds. **⚠ MY FIRST MEASUREMENT WAS WRONG — I piped the script through `grep` and read GREP's status, nearly reporting `exit=0` on a script that correctly exits 1. THE PIPE-MASKS-THE-EXIT-CODE TRAP, *THIRD TIME TONIGHT*, INSIDE THE CHECK OF A HARD-FAIL REQUIREMENT.**
> **★★ THE RULE (composer, via core) — BANKED: *A GATE IS A PROMISE ABOUT A DOWNSTREAM DECISION. ANY GATE WHOSE ACCEPTANCE SET DIFFERS FROM THE DECISION IT PROMISES ABOUT IS LYING — IN BOTH DIRECTIONS.*** The discriminator is **NOT** *"is the check structural?"* but ***"WHAT DOES THE CHECK'S OUTPUT CONTROL?"*** — **diagnostic** output ⇒ independence is right; output that **GATES passage** ⇒ it **must share the consumer's acceptance set or it lies.** ⇒ my hand-rolled walk was **RIGHT for #72** (where `parse_persona`'s blind spot WAS the defect ⇒ a second instrument was mandatory) and **WRONG for #72a** (where the question became *"will the runtime accept this aggregate?"*). **THE QUESTION MOVED AND THE INSTRUMENT DID NOT.** Already resolved in `aa9d273` — I deleted the walker before core-codex's amendment landed, for the duplicate-key divergence.
> **★ THE OVERCLAIM — CORRECTED IN CODE, AND SUPERVISOR HAD ALREADY CARRIED IT TO ROY.** Its self-correction is the sentence to keep: ***"that is on me for relaying a gate's LABEL instead of its PREDICATE."*** **A LABEL TRAVELS FURTHER THAN A PREDICATE AND ARRIVES WITH THE SAME AUTHORITY** — the overclaim was dangerous not because my log was wrong on my screen, but because it became a **true-sounding sentence in Roy's head via a lane that never read the code.** ⇒ **when relaying a gate upward, relay WHAT IT CHECKS, not what it is CALLED.** **NOW TRUE (as of e3579ce, and NOT true when it was said): an empty cert cannot reach an image on EITHER road.** **STILL NOT TRUE: that the persona's IDENTITY is verified** (#76).

> **✅✅✅ #72(a) **LANDED AND FIRED BOTH WAYS THROUGH THE REAL GATE** — rak4630-fw `50131a7` + `5a2208e` (2026-07-17). Branch-only, unpushed, nothing flashed.**
> **SHIPPED:** `crates/r2-persona-gate` = a **BUILD-ONLY helper**; private `const ANCHORS`; single public `validate_prod(persona)` (bytes only — no table param, no clock param: neither is offered because both are what an attacker or a tired operator would want to choose); build-dep on the **VENDORED** r2-trust; calls `DeviceCertificate::verify`, never reimplements. `build.rs` calls it **unconditionally** — there is no env var to leave unset, so **no absent-input branch to fail open through.**
> **★ THE ANCHOR LITERAL VERIFIES ITSELF:** `anchor_table_is_self_consistent` asserts every entry satisfies canon's `tg_id == UUID-RAW(SHA-256(tg_pk)[0:16])`. **A hardcoded 32-byte key is NOT an unverifiable literal when the table checks itself** — a typo breaks the relation and fails the build. **That was the last objection to consts, and the relation I derived from bytes this morning is what answers it.**
> **CONTROLS — THROUGH THE GATE, NOT THE PREDICATE:** **positive** = `rak-persona.bin` + anchored TG → `credential VERIFIED — tg_id=730c29e7… role=Member (TG-attested, not self-asserted)`, thumbv7em **FINISHED** · **negative** = **SAME ARTIFACT**, anchor swapped away → `REFUSING TO BAKE AN UNTRUSTED PERSONA / UnknownTrustGroup`, build **FAILED**. **Same artifact, varied anchor, both directions.** Plus **10 helper unit tests** minting a throwaway TG **in memory** (chosen AND synthetic — the correctly-scoped use of the seed rule; **no artifact exists on disk to be mistaken for an image candidate — the THIRD and cleanest kill of composer's gate-test-TG offer**): matching anchor ACCEPTS · **internally-coherent-but-FOREIGN-issuer REJECTS** (composer's face-four made concrete — *self-consistency is NOT authenticity*) · unknown TG · empty cert · cross-paired key0/key5 · window NotYetValid/ACCEPT/Expired · signature byte-flip · **key5≠anchor (constraint 4)**.
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 4 — LANDED THOUGH ALREADY CLOSED TRANSITIVELY, AND THAT IS THE POINT:** self-consistency ⇒ `key0==uuid(key5)`; lookup ⇒ `anchor.tg_id==key0`; table test ⇒ `anchor.tg_id==uuid(anchor.tg_pk)` ∴ `key5==anchor.tg_pk`. **REFUSED TO DEPEND ON IT: the middle link is a TEST not a GATE — delete the test and the proof evaporates SILENTLY while every build stays green — and the last step leans on second-preimage resistance of a 128-BIT-TRUNCATED hash.** One direct comparison needs neither. *Make the bad state unrepresentable; don't reason about why it can't arise.* Its control fires **directly** (persona self-consistent for A; table maps A's tg_id to **B's key**) so self-consistency **cannot** be what catches it.
> **★★ TWO INSTRUMENT FAILURES I CAUGHT ON MYSELF WHILE BUILDING IT — both are shapes I had banked hours earlier:** **(1) MY FIRST NEGATIVE CONTROL WAS INVALID** — the staged repeater persona failed on the **OLD #72 empty-cert check and NEVER REACHED #72a**. It has **both** defects and the earlier gate **short-circuits**. I nearly banked *"the build failed"* as proof of anchor discrimination. **Verifying logic AFTER a gate cannot catch a GATE failure — and this time the gate in front was MINE.** **(2) MY ATTRIBUTION LOG WAS A DOUBLE-COUNT** — `issuer_anchor_fp` digested the matched **KEY**, but `tg_id` **IS** `uuid(sha256(tg_pk)[0:16])`, so that fingerprint is literally the tg_id prefix. **A line whose entire purpose was INDEPENDENT attribution was restating the persona's own claim as corroboration** — **android's exact catch on composer's bind evidence, sitting UNREAD in my inbox while I made it.** Now digests the anchor **TABLE** (`fp=cd5eeb9f`): independent, and it changes when the table does.
> **★★★ NEW FINDING → TASK #75 — THE BOOTLOADER'S `0x22000` OTA TRUST ANCHOR IS COMPLETELY UNGATED.** core's constraint-4 premise was **MIS-AIMED at my gate** (it thought the bootloader's key5 was the persona my gate validates) — but **its SHAPE was right and pointed somewhere it did not follow: *"ask WHICH VALUE THE CONSUMER READS."*** Asked properly, **per consumer**: **APP (baked build) reads `BAKED_PERSONA` rodata (main.rs:490) ⇒ #72a covers it · BOOTLOADER reads FLASH `0x22000` (`r2_trust::persona_tg_pk`, bootloader main.rs:34; rak-geometry consts.rs:11 *"sealed TG_PK anchor — read by BOTH app + bootloader"*) ⇒ NOTHING COVERS IT · APP (non-baked) also reads `0x22000` ⇒ also uncovered.** **TWO DIFFERENT ARTIFACTS — different storage, different bytes, no build-time relationship.** **`0x22000` is the UPDATE AUTHORITY** and has **zero** build-time validation. **#72 closed the funnel from a bad persona to a RADIATING app; it did NOT close the funnel from a bad persona to a TRUSTED UPDATE PATH.** **UNMEASURED, DO NOT GUESS:** how is `0x22000` written? (a) same host tooling ⇒ wants the same gate · (b) only Channel-A ⇒ BOM-blocked with #74 · **(c) NOBODY ⇒ the bootloader reads an EMPTY/STALE partition as its update authority — the worst of the three.** Opened as a task rather than banking a story.
> **core's correction of MY over-correction, accepted:** *"you did not win a concession with a non-applicable argument in any way you should regret — your production argument KILLED const-in-a-shared-crate, which was correct and load-bearing. It just did not reach the helper, and NOBODY had the helper yet, so no argument in play could have."* Fair. **An argument that correctly kills the option on the table is not defective because a better option later appears outside its scope.** The regret-worthy version would be *claiming* it reaches the helper — neither of us did.

> **✅✅ #72(a) MECHANISM **RULED** — CONST IN A **BUILD-ONLY HELPER CRATE**; core REVERSED its concession and the synthesis is NEITHER lane's original (core a64e858, 2026-07-17).**
> **THE THREE-WAY RESOLUTION:** **(i) const-in-a-SHARED-crate** — killed by **my** production argument (correctly) · **(ii) env build-input** — killed by **core's** anchor-mutability argument (*"a trust anchor that can change without a commit is not an anchor"*; *"an env var is a value someone TYPES; a const is a value someone REVIEWS"*) · **(iii) CONST IN A SEPARATE BUILD-ONLY HELPER** — **beats both, and was neither of ours.** It exists **only because composer refused to let my "we settled it" stand.**
> **★★ CORE'S REVERSAL CUTS AGAINST ME AND I CONCEDE IT PLAINLY: I WON A CONCESSION WITH AN ARGUMENT THAT DOES NOT REACH THE ANSWER.** I asked core to re-examine on the production argument alone; it did and found **more than I asked** — my objection (*"a real TG's pk must not be baked into a SHARED CRATE"*) **is an argument about a SHARED RUNTIME CRATE. A build-only helper NEVER SHIPS IN THE IMAGE, so the objection does not reach it.** **And the cleaner point neither of us made: a `tg_pk` IS PUBLIC** — there was never a *secrecy* reason to keep an anchor out of a const. **The only real objection was shared-with-the-runtime, and the helper deletes it.** *An anchor is SUPPOSED to be baked and reviewed — that is what an anchor IS.*
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 1:** the helper holds the **TABLE**; **r2-trust holds the VERIFY** — the helper MUST call `DeviceCertificate::verify` and **never grow its own** (the gate's question is *"WILL THE RUNTIME ACCEPT THIS?"* — only the runtime's predicate answers it; an independent impl is a **second opinion, not a stronger one**, and it drifts).
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 2:** the const table MUST be **PRIVATE** with a **SINGLE public production entry** — *"if the validation fn is public AND takes the table as a parameter, build.rs can pass any table and you are back to a value someone types — **unswappable leaks through the parameter**."* Shape: private `const ANCHORS` · `pub fn validate_prod(persona)` taking **only** the bytes · **cfg-test injection INSIDE the helper**.
> **⚠️ MY CONSTRAINT 3 — NOT A PROPOSAL, A **LIVE DEFECT IN MY OWN CONTROLS**: THE HELPER MUST LINK THE **SAME r2-trust THE IMAGE LINKS** (the VENDORED one), AND THE MATCH MUST BE **CHECKED, NEVER ASSUMED**.** **MEASURED:** `platforms/rak4630/Cargo.toml:110` → `r2-trust = { path = "../../crates/r2-trust" }` = **VENDORED**; **my scratchpad rig linked `/home/roycdavies/Development/R2/r2-core/crates/r2-trust` = THE LIVE CORE CHECKOUT.** ⇒ **EVERY CONTROL I REPORTED FIRED AGAINST A DIFFERENT COPY OF THE CRATE THAN THE IMAGE RUNS.** Diffed after the fact: vendored `cert.rs` is **BYTE-IDENTICAL** to live ⇒ **my controls DO transfer — BY LUCK, NOT BY CONSTRUCTION.** **In THIS repo that was a live coin-flip: #71 EXISTS PRECISELY BECAUSE A VENDORED COPY IS STALE.** The vendored **dataplane** drifted; the vendored **r2-trust** happened not to. **⇒ MY CONCLUSION SURVIVES; MY METHOD DID NOT ESTABLISH IT.** And **#71 will MOVE the vendored copy — today's match is not tomorrow's.** Core's constraint 1 *implies* this but doesn't say it, and the implication is where it bites: **a wrong path in a manifest silently converts the gate's question into *"will SOME runtime accept this?"*** See [[shared-checkout-path-dep-coupling]], [[tn-base-is-mixed-sha-assembly]].
> **OPEN INTERACTION (asked core to rule): `validate_prod` must select WHICH anchor by the persona's OWN `tg_id` (key0) — *the input choosing its own judge*, the family we hunted all night.** **My read: SAFE** — selecting a *legitimate* table anchor doesn't help an attacker who cannot forge a signature for a TG whose sk they lack; the lookup picks the judge, but the judge is incorruptible. **BUT ⇒ `validate_prod(persona)` ALONE CANNOT ENFORCE "this image is for TG X"** — any persona whose tg_id is in the table builds fine. **That is exactly what `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID` is for, and it lands on core's OWN split: the ANCHOR = private const (unswappable, absence = compile error); the EXPECTATION = env var in build.rs (optional but LOUD when unset). Two legs, two mechanisms, for a principled reason — only the ANCHOR may not be typeable.**
> **✅ CORE'S REVOCATION WITHDRAWAL — CONFIRMED FROM MY OWN MEASUREMENT:** the custody record for `730c29e7` shows **`members[] len = 4`** and **`sealed_tg_sk` PRESENT** ⇒ a **four-member TG with a held signing key** ⇒ *"a singleton TG has no revocation path"* is **FALSE of the live TG** and **TRUE of the staged repeater `<REDACTED-custody>`**. **The 3650-day argument keeps the limb that carries** (30d is ALREADY the extended case, extended for the NAMED reason *"to cover shipping"*, and the clause's second half — renew on first mesh connectivity — means a 10-year cert **DEFEATS THE MECHANISM THE SHOULD EXISTS TO ENABLE**) **and drops the limb that does not.** core carried the withdrawal rather than let the stronger argument smuggle it.
> **NEXT (unblocked, branch-only): implement (iii)** — build-only helper crate · private `const ANCHORS` · single public `validate_prod(persona)` · cfg-test injection inside the helper · **build-dep on the VENDORED r2-trust** · calls `DeviceCertificate::verify`, never reimplements. **Both controls RE-RUN THROUGH THE GATE, not against the predicate** — *I proved the PREDICATE and refused to claim the GATE, and that gap stays open until the gate exists.*

> **🛑🛑 MY 2026-08-28 IS **VOID** AND MY 07-22 HARD COMMIT IS **CANCELLED** — I SPIKED THE WRONG ROOT, AND CANON HAD ALREADY RULED THIS PART FOR FOUR DAYS (2026-07-17).**
> **R2-KEYSTORE §9:463-485 requires ALL THREE hardware roots for a PERSISTENT CLAIM-STATE profile:** **(a)** irreversible OTP VIRGIN sentinel · **(b)** a **DEDICATED MONOTONIC HARDWARE `hw_epoch` COUNTER** — canon's words, ***"the SOLE anti-rollback and linearisation root"*** · **(c)** a per-device HUK/SE key from which `K_slot` **AND** `K_persona` derive. **§9:485 verbatim: *"A platform lacking ANY of these three roots MUST FAIL CLOSED at build / provision time."***
> **MY SPIKE #73 ASKED ABOUT (c). THE PART CANON-LACKS (b).** **VERIFIED MYSELF FROM SPEC TEXT** (two lanes were citing canon at me; after tonight I take neither's say-so): **§9:489-492** — *"parts without an on-die OTP monotonic counter — **e.g. nRF52840/RAK4630** — MUST pair an external secure element (ATECC608 / NervesKey / TPM) … **else they are non-persistent-only**"* · **R2-UPDATE §9.2:1119** — *"**Honest platform delta — nRF52840 has NO HW-OTP counter (the RAK4630 backend).**"* · **§9** — *"There is **NO software-only persistent claim-state**; hardware-where-available is **NOT permitted**."*
> **⇒ EVEN A PERFECT POSITIVE ON (c) CHANGES NOTHING** — the part still lacks (b), remedy is the same external SE either way. **THE SPIKE COULD ONLY CHANGE *WHICH* ROOT I'M MISSING, NEVER THE OUTCOME.** Channel-A **IS** a persistent claim-state profile (§5.1.1 stages at `hw_epoch+1` → marker → **increments `hw_epoch`** = root (b)). **⇒ CONFORMANT-PERSISTENT CHANNEL-A ON A BARE RAK4630 IS A *ROY BOM DECISION*, NOT AN ENGINEERING SCHEDULE.** Canon defers the per-board matrix to *"a **Roy-gated R2-HW reconciliation**"*. **No date until Roy rules the BOM.**
> **★★★ THE SPLIT I HAD CONFLATED — THE MOST USEFUL THING IN THE THREAD: *(A)-CONFORMANT AND THE DEMO ARE DIFFERENT DELIVERABLES AND ONLY ONE IS BOM-BLOCKED.* The demo needs A WORKING RELAY; a relay needs NO persistent claim-state at all.** Canon explicitly permits the fallback — **§9:486-488**: *"A **bench / development** build MAY run **explicitly non-persistent** (claim-state not retained across power-cycle — never a field or production profile)"* = **supervisor's NON-PERSISTENT-ONLY waiver term. CANON NAMED OUR FALLBACK BEFORE WE DID.** ⇒ **Roy's (B) + non-persistent-only carries the bench demo TODAY, zero BOM dependency. DO NOT let my missing (A) date block the demo — they were never the same thing.** **NOT the risk: the engineering** (§5.1.1 byte-frozen + pv-1 vectors). **THE SILICON WAS THE RISK, NOT THE WIRE.**
> **★★ MY ERROR SHAPE, and it is the family that fired all night: I SPIKED THE ROOT I HAPPENED TO BE THINKING ABOUT, NOT THE ROOT THAT BINDS.** I framed the question; both cores answered *the question I asked*; **only the fork asked whether it was the RIGHT question.** **The fix was never a harder spike — it was reading the spec that already ruled it.** Canon had named this exact part, twice, for four days. See [[never-conclude-from-a-null]].
> **★★★ THE OFF-THREAD FORK HAZARD *INVERTED* — core's warning about its own copy was exactly backwards, and this is worth more than the seal-root answer.** core warned: *"if the off-thread copy gave you a flat negative WITHOUT that caveat, **it gave you MORE confidence than I have**."* **THE OPPOSITE:** the **fork REFUSED** the silicon question (*"I DON'T KNOW, I have no verified evidence, and I'm not going to reason from recollection about silicon — that's circuits' lane"*) and answered **from canon text**; the **LIVE** core **reasoned from silicon architecture** (no KMU / volatile KDR / APPROTECT glitch-bypass) and *then* caveated it. **⇒ THE FORK WAS MORE DISCIPLINED THAN THE ORIGINAL AND FOUND THE BINDING ROOT (b) THE LIVE ANSWER MISSED ENTIRELY (its answer is all root (c) — never mentions the counter).** **Both said NEGATIVE; only the fork was negative for the reason that BINDS** ⇒ **core's own "right answer, wrong reason" rule firing inside core's own live answer**: its verdict is **over-determined** but it **mortgaged it to the one leg that needs circuits**, while canon's root-(b) leg needs nobody. **⇒ I do NOT need circuits for the date** (still worth asking for its own sake; **not** a blocker). **DO NOT assume a fork is a DEGRADED copy — here it was the better one. The real hazard is the one core named: YOU CANNOT AUDIT WHAT IT SAID.**
> **FICR.DEVICEID REFUSAL — STANDS, CANON-BACKED, and the fork's form beats both mine and core's:** (c) must be a per-device **KEY**; a **readable IKM** ⇒ `K_persona` computable by anyone who can read the ID ⇒ **it COLLAPSES §5.1.1's ENTIRE PREMISE** — composer *cannot* construct the device-sealed bytes **because** it lacks the root; with a readable root **composer COULD**, and the property the whole transaction is built on **evaporates**. **The seal doesn't merely leak — it STOPS BEING A SEAL.**
> **✅ `730c29e7` (the LIVE demo TG) — CLOSED: NO documented seed, it is OsRng.** composer's custody route was **INCONCLUSIVE and it SAID SO** (*"my control did NOT fire"* — tg.txt stores hex not seeds; no custody record for 730c29e7 on its box). **The proof that carries is STRUCTURAL and I VERIFIED IT: `f906a93` created the seed capability TODAY (2026-07-17); `rak-persona.bin`'s cert `issued_at` = 1783974862 = 2026-07-13 20:34 UTC = FOUR DAYS EARLIER.** ***An artifact cannot be produced by a capability that does not yet exist.*** ⇒ **"publicly controllable by construction" is FALSE of the live demo. Nobody holds `730c29e7`'s key.** (Same run confirms the 3650-day window: expires 2036-07-10.)
> **★★ composer's CAPSTONE — THE SAME COIN AS MINE, ONE LAYER DOWN: *the OsRng-ness that was the DEFECT this morning is exactly what makes the live TG SAFE from the thing I found tonight.*** CHOSEN-SEED = **auditable** AND **publicly controllable**; OsRng = **not auditable** AND **not publicly controllable**. **ONE PROPERTY — *is the key derivable from published information* — read from two ends**, exactly my const/env coin. *"I counted the favourable end of one coin and called it a safety property; you counted the favourable end of another and called it two coins. Same error, same night, in both directions."*
> **⚠️ FOR supervisor+core (composer's finding, MY rule turned on THEIR remedy): the f906a93 requirement — *"MUST be synthetic-by-construction from a CHOSEN DOCUMENTED SEED anyone can recompute"* — IS SCOPED TO WORTHLESS IDENTITIES AND IS **NOT A GENERAL RULE**. APPLIED TO A REAL IDENTITY IT WOULD PUBLISH THE PRODUCTION KEY.** If anyone reads f906a93 as *"always use a documented seed"* and points it at a production TG, **the remedy becomes the catastrophe.** *A remedy is scoped to the context that justified it; diagnosis transfers, treatment does not.* **The requirement needs its scope written into it or it is a loaded gun pointed at the first production TG.** Escalated.

> **⚠️⚠️ MY "BUILD-INPUT PAID FOR ITSELF TWICE" IS **KILLED** — composer's catch, CONCEDED WITHOUT QUALIFICATION; core asked to UN-BANK it (2026-07-17).** *"The mechanism that makes the gate TESTABLE is the one that makes it FAIL-OPEN; the mechanism that makes it FAIL-CLOSED is the one whose negative control needs a code edit. **That is the SAME PROPERTY READ FROM TWO ENDS — a TRADE, not a dividend.**"* **Correct.** The single property = **can the anchor change without a commit?** mutable ⇒ testable **AND** fail-open-prone; immutable ⇒ auditable **AND** test needs a code edit. **I counted the favourable end of ONE coin and called it TWO coins.** **★ THE SYMMETRY IS DAMNING: that is the IDENTICAL error composer confessed ONE MESSAGE EARLIER** about its own seed (*"RECOMPUTABLE ⇒ ANYONE CAN RECOMPUTE ⇒ ANYONE HOLDS THE KEY — the same property from opposite ends, and **I only ever wrote the flattering half**"*). **It caught me doing what it had just confessed.** ⇒ **core said *"the argument I conceded to was WEAKER than the case actually is"* — NO: THE CASE IS WEAKER THAN I CLAIMED.** Re-examine the concession on the **production argument alone**; I don't want a ruling won with a bad coin.
> **THE CONST-vs-BUILD-INPUT CONTRADICTION WAS *MY RELAY ERROR*, not fleet drift.** T1: core ruled **CONST-in-a-shared-crate** → I relayed it → **composer withdrew its env recommendation on my relay.** T2: **core CONCEDED to build-input** on my production argument → **I never sent composer the reversal**, then announced *"settled"*. **⇒ composer sits on CONST and core on BUILD-INPUT and I put them both there.** composer was right to refuse *"we settled it"* — and refused it **exactly where its own position had been overturned an hour earlier.**
> **WHAT SURVIVES / WHAT DOESN'T:** I **already paid the fail-open end** (anchor UNCONDITIONAL — absent ⇒ **build FAILURE**, not skip) ⇒ *"the natural implementation of an absent env var is skip-the-check"* is true of the **natural** impl, **false of mine**. **BUT core's OTHER limb SURVIVES and sha-logging does NOT answer it:** *"a trust anchor that can change without a commit is not an anchor"* — set `RAK_ISSUER_PK` wrong and my gate **validates against the wrong anchor and reports SUCCESS**; logging makes that **detectable-after-the-fact, not impossible**. *An env var is a value someone TYPES; a const is a value someone REVIEWS.*
> **✅ MEASURED (not asserted) — A BUILD SCRIPT DOES NOT SEE `cfg(test)`.** composer's resolution (const table + `#[cfg(test)]` extra entry) **cannot reach a build.rs gate as written**: throwaway crate prints **DOES-NOT-SEE under BOTH `cargo test` AND `cargo build`** (control: the **library** DOES see it). **⇒ THE SHAPE THAT DISSOLVES THE TRADE (core's call, I propose not decide): anchor TABLE + validation in a SEPARATE HELPER CRATE, taken by build.rs as a build-DEPENDENCY.** Production = **const table, diff-visible, reviewed, unswappable, absence = COMPILE ERROR, fail-closed on unknown tg_id**; Tests = **the HELPER's own suite injects a test anchor via `cfg(test)`** ⇒ both controls free, no code edit, no env hole. **core's fail-closed AND composer's testability, no trade — a shape neither of them named, which exists only because composer refused my "settled".**

Same artifact + **correct** anchor: flip **last sig byte** → REJECT(Signature) · flip **first sig byte** → REJECT(Signature) · flip a **cert DATA byte** → REJECT(Signature). ⇒ **verify checks the BYTES, not just the key.** Core's named residual closed **on the axis it named** — and **I would not have run it.**

The rule is NEVER LET A TRUNCATION SIT UPSTREAM OF A MATCHER — not "avoid cut".** **★ core's lesson banked: *"A REFUTATION THAT FLATTERS YOUR HUMILITY IS STILL A CLAIM — I deferred because CONCEDING FELT LIKE RIGOUR."*** = deference-is-a-refutation-failure in its most convincing disguise. **OWED: re-check my build.rs comments and correct BACK — ~30d IS canon (SHOULD @:427).**

> **⚖️ SUPERVISOR'S SEED SPLIT — REFUTED (chosen-vs-derived is the WRONG TEST HERE).** It proposed: TG seed = published-by-design (rule 8 recomputability), master seed = the real leak. **BOTH are the same class and it is the LEAK class.** **(1) CHOSEN ≠ SYNTHETIC — two axes collapsed:** CHOSEN-vs-RANDOM = how bytes are GENERATED; SYNTHETIC-vs-REAL = what they PROTECT. **Determinism doesn't make a key fake — it makes it reproducible, which is exactly what makes publishing the seed identical to publishing the key.** **(2) The contrast class is in MY OWN RESUME:** `uuid(0x42*32)` / `hive(0xAA*32)` = chosen **AND** synthetic (no board runs them) ⇒ *those* are rule-8 artifacts; the repeater TG is **chosen-but-LIVE** (minted to be baked; it WAS staged `ee3b7791`). **(3) GROUND TRUTH composer does NOT treat it as published-by-design:** its own `tg.txt` header says **"SENSITIVE: tg_sk + master secrets in plaintext"**; it lives in **mode-600 custody**, not a docs dir; composer's own words — its derivation *"needs a custody-unlocked run"*. **(4) THE KILLER — rule 8 does NOT compel publishing this seed: recomputability requires the PUBLIC key be checkable, and VERIFYING A PUBLIC KEY NEVER REQUIRES PUBLISHING THE GENERATOR OF THE PRIVATE ONE.** tg_pk could have been handed directly (it already sits in this file classified public). **The auditability requirement is satisfied ONE BIT SHORT of the disclosure.** **(5) The split is unstable — siblings from one file, same construction/batch/custody: applied consistently it makes both benign (false) or both leaks (true).**

>       - **★ THE ELF SHA IS *NOT* A SUFFICIENT ANCHOR** (this RETRACTS the earlier "ELF sha IS the handoff anchor" agreement). composer canon (catalogue/recipes/_README.md:72-73 + nrf52840-rak4630.hive.toml:48-59) requires **THREE DISTINCT DIGESTS**: **`image_digest`** = sha256 of the RAW **.bin ON FLASH at 0x26000** (the container-independent tamper anchor a device read-back reproduces); **`flash_package_digest`** = sha256 of the **DFU .zip the tool CONSUMES**; **`hex_container_digest`** = sha256 of the Intel-HEX container. An ELF sha pins only the **INPUT** — it CANNOT catch **objcopy offset drift** (app MUST sit at 0x26000) or **genpkg packaging drift**. **STAGE + REPORT `image_digest` (.bin) AND `flash_package_digest` (.zip), not just the ELF sha.**
>       - **EXACT ROUTE (no slash/ambiguity): adafruit-nrfutil SERIAL-DFU** (FLASH-RECIPE.md:18-28). Consumed artifact = the **DFU .zip** — NOT .uf2, NOT .elf. Pipeline: **elf → hex (app @0x26000) → DFU .zip → serial DFU**. Ignore the UF2 branch for this op.

> **★ CORE'S "INVERTED RISK" RE-INVERTED — THE STAGED RAK IS *NOT* DEAF (verified at source, positive-controlled, 2026-07-17).** core retracted its sx1262 clobber-fear (direction misread — matching my independent finding) and replaced it with: *"the danger is the STAGED FIRMWARE IS RUNNING WITHOUT core's duty-cycle/RX-arming path."* **TRUE as stated, MIS-STATED as a risk.** Vendored r2-sx1262 has `SET_RX = 0x82` (continuous SetRx), `fn listen()` :525 ("enable the RX path (RXEN HIGH) before SetRx"), `fn read()` :554 → RxInfo; main.rs RX loop = `radio.poll()` → `RadioEvent::RxDone` → `radio.read()` → `handle_rx_frame(..., PHY_LORA, ...)`. **A complete, working CONTINUOUS RX path.** core's `listen_duty_cycle`/`set_rx_standby`/`set_rx_continuous` are the **SetRxDutyCycle (0x94) POWER-SAVING** path — an enhancement; missing them costs POWER, not hearing. **⇒ THE RISK INVERTS AGAIN: for a USB-powered bench, CONTINUOUS RX is the SAFER mode (it cannot miss); duty-cycled RX would ADD the [[setrxdutycycle-preamble-sizing]] hazard (rxPeriod+sleepPeriod ≤ TX preamble airtime, else HARD-MISS). Recommendation: take the APIs in a snapshot if we escalate, but do NOT enable duty-cycled RX for the demo.** Corroborated by history: first light RAN; nbrs=0 was SF-attributable (DFR SF7 vs RAK SF12) ⇒ RX was alive, hence **benchsf7 MANDATORY**.

>   - **`listen_duty_cycle`: 0 @1275732 → 9 @bd563fd = upstream ADD, ABSENT in vendored** (1275732 IS an ancestor of `1bbb32b`, where it entered). **My "core's own at 1275732, later REMOVED" is FALSE for the duty-cycle APIs.**

>   - **★ THE STING: `1bbb32b` = "SetRxDutyCycle 0x94 — hardware RX duty-cycle mode (HIVE-PROPOSED, core-accepted)" — the API I mischaracterised as "core's own, later removed" is MY OWN PROPOSAL.** I misread the history of my own contribution; a prior belief ("sx1262 duty-cycle = core's area") made the diff oblige. See [[setrxdutycycle-preamble-sizing]] — I literally hold the memory for this feature.
>   - **VERDICT STANDS (pristine@1275732, core-lineage, replace-safe, nothing to upstream) — it was OVER-DETERMINED by the lineage check and never rested on the mechanism.** RX re-inversion also stands on the TRUE direction: the vendored genuinely LACKS 0x94 (absence, not clobber) but is NOT deaf — SET_RX 0x82 continuous via `listen()`+`poll()`+`read()`. Absence costs POWER-SAVING, not hearing; and **absence of 0x94 is the SAFE state for a USB bench** (continuous cannot miss; 0x94 mis-sized ⇒ HARD-MISS).
>   - **★★ CORE'S EPISTEMIC POINT — BANKED (the best formulation in the thread): "recording a wrong REASON would make a later refutation of the MECHANISM look like a refutation of the VERDICT."** ⇒ **a right answer for a wrong reason is a LIABILITY, not a win: it mortgages a sound verdict against a premise that cannot carry it.** Mine was exactly that — pure unforced risk on an already over-determined conclusion. **Correct the reason even when the answer holds.**


> **▶▶ REBUILD REQUIREMENTS — PINNED BY SUPERVISOR (2026-07-17). Three, all load-bearing, all already in the runbook; consolidated here so they are not scattered:**
>   1. **`benchsf7` IS MANDATORY — it is the THIRD SILENT-FAILURE GATE.** Evidence (my first-light corroboration, which supervisor made the key fact): the RAK's `nbrs=0` was **SF-ATTRIBUTABLE** (DFR SF7 vs RAK SF12) — **the RX path was ALIVE and heard nothing purely from the SF mismatch.** ⇒ **without `benchsf7` the RAK is DEAF regardless of a perfect compact decode.** **The three silent gates each produce "no reading" with NO error: (a) compact decode [the RED], (b) the bridge leg [REFUTED — XIAO is compact-native], (c) SF match [benchsf7].** All three must hold; any one fails silently. See [[shared-radio-config-is-a-base-not-a-guarantee]].
>   2. **Do NOT ENABLE duty-cycled RX on the bench — stay CONTINUOUS.** Take core's 0x94 APIs as part of a snapshot; **do not turn them on.** SX1262 0x94 requires `(rxPeriod + sleepPeriod) <= TX preamble airtime` or **HARD-MISS**; on USB power continuous RX **cannot miss**, so duty-cycling would ADD a failure mode we do not have. [[setrxdutycycle-preamble-sizing]].
>   3. **WHOLE TREES + REGENERATE the workspace lock from the PINNED MANIFESTS.** core's manifest point is material: firmware r2-trust/r2-engine manifests match their OLDER bases (3e15d75/fbee20d) ⇒ **new src on an old manifest = missing dep/feature** (core has ed25519-dalek `features=[rand_core]`; r2-engine adds `sha2`).

> **🛑 MY FIRMWARE'S PERSONA PATH FAILS OPEN INTO RADIATION — REAL PRE-FLASH DEFECT (core's find; composer refuted my softening; NOT closed as not-hit).** build.rs:96-107 embeds `$RAK_PERSONA_PATH` bytes RAW with **no parse/identity validation**; main.rs:776-801 maps parse-failure → `DataPlane::new(..., None, ...)` labelled *"§3.5 persona ABSENT → FAIL-CLOSED keyless repeater"* and **CONTINUES INTO RADIO SERVICE**. It is fail-closed for **DELIVERY** but **fail-OPEN for IDENTITY**: a wrong/corrupt persona silently yields a **RADIATING KEYLESS RELAY**, violating Roy's ABSOLUTE no-TG-less canon ("there is no device with group = none") + forbidden-to-radiate.
>   - **★ I TRIED TO SOFTEN THIS AND COMPOSER CAUGHT ME — I WALKED INTO MY OWN RULE.** I wrote *"the fail-OPEN path exists but was NOT TAKEN"* (citing my ELF proof). [[never-conclude-from-a-null]] says verbatim: *"we UNDER-AUDIT DE-ESCALATIONS because they lower the stakes… a softening claim needs the SAME positive control as a hardening one… applies to my own de-escalations too."* **I wrote the rule, then did the thing — on my OWN firmware's defect, where the incentive to soften is highest.** composer, verbatim: *"a fail-OPEN that happens to be fed good input is still fail-open; the next build is the one that bites."* **Correct: my ELF proof is an IDENTITY fact about THIS artifact; the defect is a CONTROL-FLOW fact. Separate axes ([[identity-verified-is-not-function-verified]] again). The image is confirmed keyed AND the defect is confirmed real; neither weakens the other.**

> **🛑🛑🛑 FLASH-BLOCKER — THE STAGED PERSONA HAS AN EMPTY CERTIFICATE. `ee3b7791` WAS NEVER FLASHABLE. (core-codex filed, core re-derived, I VERIFIED FROM THE BYTES, 2026-07-17.)**
>   - **MEASURED (my own independent hand-decode of the 188B `persona-rak-repeater.bin`):** `a7` map(7); key `0x00` text(36) tg_id; `0x01/0x02/0x03` bytes(32) dek/hk/master; **★ key `0x04` → header `0x40` = bytes(0) = EMPTY CERT**; `0x05` bytes(32) tg_pk; `0x06` uint. **NEGATIVE CONTROL — and it sat in the SAME DIRECTORY the whole time: `rak-persona.bin` / `d4-persona.bin` / `xiao-persona.bin` (336B each) ALL carry key04 = `04 58 93` = bytes(147) = a real cert147.** `336-188 = 148` = exactly the missing cert + header — the arithmetic confirms the decode.
>   - **★★★ WHY MY "EXEMPLARY" 3-WAY PROOF MISSED IT — THE DEEPEST LESSON OF THE CAMPAIGN, and it detonated MY OWN RULE ON MY OWN FLAGSHIP PROOF.** `tg_hash`/`wire_id`/`rbid` **all derive from key0 (tg_id) + key3 (master) (+ key2 hk)**. So my confirm-match ranged over keys **0/1/2/3/5** and was **STRUCTURALLY INCAPABLE** of saying anything about **key 4**. core's formulation, exactly right: **"A PROOF THAT THE GOOD FIELDS ARE GOOD IS NOT A PROOF THAT THE BAD FIELD IS ABSENT."** **My positive control DID fire — on the wrong fields.** ⇒ **SCOPE-IS-PART-OF-THE-METHOD, sharpened: a positive control must fire ON THE FIELD IN QUESTION, not merely somewhere in the artifact.** I taught the fleet that rule tonight; my flagship proof violated it, and three lanes (supervisor "exemplary", composer "the model", core "the right kind of evidence") all praised it — **peer praise is not coverage.**
>   - **★ COMPOUNDING — THE INSTRUMENT WAS THE BLIND SPOT: my verification tool was `r2_trust::parse_persona`, and it returns `Ok` on an empty cert.** The tool I verified WITH is the tool that CANNOT SEE the defect. ⇒ core's fix is the right SHAPE: **require cert147 BY TYPE so an empty cert is UNREPRESENTABLE — a CONSTRUCTION, not a check** ([[never-conclude-from-a-null]]'s "convert convention → construction"). **It makes my old proof impossible to write.** core's hardened parser will make the CURRENT artifact FAIL TO PARSE — that is the point; re-mint and fix land together.
>   - **★ IDENTITY, THIRD AXIS, SAME DAY: identity ≠ FUNCTION (the compact silent-drop) · identity ≠ CONTROL-FLOW (the fail-open) · identity ≠ COMPLETENESS (this).** I proved the persona **IS** the right identity; never that it is a **COMPLETE** persona. **One artifact, three axes, and I kept re-verifying the axis I had already verified.** [[identity-verified-is-not-function-verified]].
>   - **SAME WOUND AS #72:** build.rs embeds `RAK_PERSONA_PATH` **raw, no parse** (:96-107) ⇒ an invalid persona is embedded silently; main.rs then maps parse-failure → **RADIATING KEYLESS relay** (:778-789 logs VALID + enables GroupHmac). **A persona invalid in a way `parse_persona` cannot see is the worst case of both.**
>   - **3-LANE INTERLOCK: composer RE-MINTS with cert147 · core HARDENS `parse_persona` (cert147 by type) · I add the runtime FAIL-STOP before radio configure + build-time expected-identity validation + a direct-from-image cert147 assert (verify the ARTIFACT, not the mint) — task #72.** **ASKED supervisor for sequencing (I want #72 FIRST + standalone — pure safety, needs no pin, must be true before ANY flash — then the re-vendor transplant on top; both touch build.rs+main.rs).** **Asked core to confirm the composition: my fail-stop needs its hardened parser to have something to trip on — and I argued for BOTH (its type-level construction AND my artifact-level assert; they fail differently).** **NOT writing firmware into a 3-lane interlock while the HOLD is live.**


> **✅ CARRIER-ID PROVENANCE — RE-RUN, MEASUREMENT NOT MEMORY (2026-07-17; supervisor's ask, and it was the right one).** supervisor honestly corrected ITS OWN overstatement to Roy ("CONFIRMED REAL FROM THE MEASUREMENT" when I had plainly said I answered from my ARCHIVED RECORD) and asked me to **re-run rather than rely on a 2-week-old method — because I made three method-scope errors TODAY, so my own old method deserves the same doubt.** Correct, and it survives:
>   - **HARNESS: `scratchpad/derivemap`** — a cargo bin on the **REAL crate** `r2-trust` (features=[std]). NOT a re-implementation; NOT the original `persona_map.py` (session-scoped scratchpad, gone) ⇒ **re-running against the canonical crate is STRONGER than re-running my old script.**
>   - **DERIVATION:** `parse_persona() → Persona.hive_id`, computed internally per **hkdf.rs:145** `derive_hive_id(master_secret, tg_id) = fnv1a_32(uuid(HKDF(master,"r2-hive-id-v1",tg_id)[0:16]))` ⇒ **hive_id is DERIVED from key3(master)+key0(tg_id), never stored.**
>   - **POSITIVE CONTROL FIRED FIRST:** derive(RAK repeater) = `<REDACTED-custody>` = expected ⇒ harness proven able to produce a known-correct answer. **RESULT: 5 custody personas derived; the disputed carrier id IS in the derived set ⇒ derived from a REAL custody master_secret ⇒ REAL, on today's evidence.** No secrets/MACs/ids emitted — membership + counts only.
>   - **NULL EXPLAINED (never leave one dangling):** the "1 failed to parse" = `weave-hk.bin`, a 32-byte RAW HK swept in by my `*.bin` filter. Benign. **AND I HIT COMPOSER'S TRAP MYSELF, HOURS AFTER BANKING IT: my custody listing used `ls | head -10` — the head had hidden the very file that produced the null.** Re-ran with `wc -l`: 6 files.
> **★★ ROOT CAUSE OF THE EMPTY-CERT FLASH-BLOCKER — TWO PERSONA FORMATS, and the difference IS the cert:** **188B ⇒ key04 = `04 40` = bytes(0) EMPTY** · **336B ⇒ key04 = `04 58 93` = bytes(147) cert147**. `~/r2-weave-tg` = **5 × 188B, ALL empty-cert** (on the weave boards since Jul 2); `~/.r2-dev-trial` rak/d4/xiao = **336B, real cert147**; **composer's new chosen-seed repeater persona (Jul 16) = 188B, EMPTY.** ⇒ **the replacement came out of the SAME no-cert generation path as the old weave set — NOT a corrupt file, NOT a one-off: a GENERATION-PATH difference.** Fix belongs there; and the **ARTIFACT** must be checked (336B + key04 `04 58 93`) before staging — **verify the artifact, not the process.**
>   - **⚠ THE UNCOMFORTABLE COROLLARY: the weave boards have run EMPTY-CERT personas since Jul 2 and nothing broke ⇒ NOTHING CURRENTLY VERIFIES THE CERT.** `parse_persona` returns Ok because an empty cert parses to **`Some(&[])`, not `None`**. **That is why core's fix must be BY TYPE (unrepresentable), not another check: the cert is currently DECORATIVE, so every check that could have caught this was structurally incapable of it — mine included.**
