> **✅✅ TASK #72 LANDED — THE FAIL-OPEN-INTO-RADIATION FUNNEL IS CLOSED (rak4630-fw `56f6cae`, branch-only, no push, no flash, 2026-07-17).** supervisor GO'd the sequencing (**#72 FIRST + standalone, re-vendor on top** — *"the hold was on the re-vendor and the flash; it was never a hold on safety work in your own repo"*); core ruled the composition (**BOTH layers**).
>   - **(1) build.rs VALIDATE-BEFORE-EMBED** — hand-rolled CBOR walk, **deliberately NOT via `parse_persona`**. core's reason and it is the crux: *that parser returns `Ok` on an empty cert, so the instrument used to verify the artifact was constitutionally unable to report the defect — a defence-in-depth layer whose only check routes through the component that already had the blind spot is not defence in depth.* Rejects: non-map / truncated / missing key0|key4 / **EMPTY cert (key4=`0x40`)** / non-bytes cert / wrong tg_id vs optional `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID`. **Build fails.**
>   - **(2) main.rs HARD STOP** — the invalid arm now **DIVERGES** instead of building a keyless DataPlane and falling through to `radio.configure()` ~10 lines below ⇒ **"never radiate" is true BY CONSTRUCTION (compiler-proven no path), not by convention.** **Async loop, NOT `panic!`** — executor stays alive so USB-CDC log + LED stay observable with no probe and USB-DFU re-provisioning still works; a panic would take the log down and leave a dark board with no reason on the wire.
>   - **★ VERIFIED WITH REAL CONTROLS — I tested my own gate the way I have been demanding others test theirs, against REAL artifacts:** **NEGATIVE:** the ACTUAL staged empty-cert persona (188B) ⇒ **BUILD FAILS** (*"REFUSING TO BAKE AN INVALID PERSONA / CERTIFICATE IS EMPTY (key 4 = 0x40 = bytes(0))"*) — the gate fires on the exact artifact that was staged and nearly flashed. **POSITIVE:** real cert147 persona (336B) ⇒ *"validated (336 bytes, certificate present) — baking"*, no false-positive. **COMPILE:** clean, thumbv7em, 11.17s. *(A gate reporting OK is not evidence until its KATs prove it catches the thing — so I proved it catches THE thing.)*
>   - **OWED, NAMED IN-FILE (explicit, not implied): (a) cert SIGNATURE + validity WINDOW at BUILD time** — core-codex's catch: feeding the **untrusted bundle's own `issued_at`** into a verifier = **expiry self-authorized**. build.rs is the only place with a trusted clock. **⚠ MECHANISM — MY ANSWER WAS OVERRULED BY CORE, AND CORE IS RIGHT. IT IS A CONST IN A SHARED CRATE, NOT AN ENV PATH.** ~~BUILD INPUT = env path~~ **REFUTED**: (i) *an env path is the `RAK_PERSONA_PATH` trap one level up* — a value nobody reviews, a file nobody diffed, **which is HOW the empty cert got in**; (ii) **the natural implementation of an absent env var is SKIP THE CHECK = a FAIL-OPEN BY DEFAULT in the gate whose whole job is to fail closed**, failing silently and looking exactly like success; (iii) **"an env var is a value someone TYPES; a const is a value someone REVIEWS"** — git-auditable, diff-visible, unswappable per-build, and **absence is a COMPILE ERROR, not a skipped branch**; (iv) composer's production objection is answered by a **const TABLE keyed by tg_id, fail-closed on unknown** — and **"if a new TG needs a commit to add its anchor, THAT IS THE FEATURE: a trust anchor that can change without a commit is not an anchor."** **★ THE DECIDING CONSTRAINT (core-codex) — NEVER verify the cert against the persona's OWN key 5:** the baked app carries tg_pk+cert+hk+dek+master together in plaintext, so that proves only **SELF-CONSISTENCY** — an image replacement swaps BOTH and still passes. **The issuer key MUST come from OUTSIDE the bundle.** ⇒ **THIS KILLS composer's "issuer pk = its tg_pk" OFFER, WHICH I HAD ACCEPTED — one message after banking the rule that forbids it ("an untrusted input trusted to describe itself; never let an input supply the predicate that judges it"). Third time today I banked a rule and violated it on the next claim (direction-misread → wrong-board → this). The rule is not the hard part; APPLYING it to the thing in front of me is.** composer's *recomputability* argument survives but does not save it: **seed-derivability makes the const AUDITABLE to a REVIEWER; it does not make the bundle AUTHENTIC to the VERIFIER.** Right property, wrong risk. — in PRODUCTION the issuer is a REAL TG whose pk must NOT be baked into a shared crate, and a dev-trial shortcut becomes the production shape by default unless refused up front; dev-trial supplies its value THROUGH the general mechanism. **composer IS the issuer, and the key is PUBLIC + RECOMPUTABLE**: the repeater-TG cert issuer is the repeater TG ⇒ issuer pk = its `tg_pk` = the ed25519 verifying key of `tg_sk = SHA-256('<TG-SEED — REDACTED: this string IS the TG key; custody-only>')`. ⇒ composer's decisive line: **"a hardcoded const would be an UNVERIFIABLE literal; a documented-seed-derived const is a CHECKABLE one"** — a literal I cannot recompute is a literal I cannot audit (the rbid-resolve.py property, applied to the issuer). **★ NOT LANDING IT UNTIL I CAN FIRE IT BOTH WAYS** (a matching pk must ACCEPT, a wrong pk must REJECT): the repeater persona has NO cert yet (that IS the flash-blocker), and rak-persona.bin's cert is from a DIFFERENT TG ⇒ a negative-control candidate only. **(a) lands WITH composer's cert-bearing persona, both controls fired — building it blind and calling it done is the identical error I just conceded.** R2-PROVISION:324 (NOT R2-RUNTIME — core relayed the wrong number, specs caught it, I propagated it) = signature ALWAYS, expiry only where offline-checkable; **no-clock never excuses a bad signature**. **(b) runtime strict STRUCTURAL decode (no clock)** — lands with core's hardened `parse_persona` (cert147 by type); my fail-stop turns its `Err` into the hard stop. **(c) NOT VERIFIED: on-metal runtime** (no board) — the no-path-to-radio property is **compiler-checked, not observed**; claiming no more than that.
>   - **INTERLOCK:** composer re-produces the persona via the **cert-bearing** path (**188B = the known-bad no-cert generation path** — same one that made the 5 old weave personas, all empty-cert; **good = ~336B, key04 = `0x58 0x93` = bytes(147)**), **held pending a specs ROLE ruling — and composer is right to hold: a wrong-role cert PARSES and radiates; an empty one now fails loudly at build.** That asymmetry is why the role question outranks the empty cert. **#71 transplant lands ON TOP of this and gets re-touched exactly once — which is why safety-first was the right sequence.**


> **⚠⚠ I BUILT A FAIL-OPEN INTO THE FAIL-CLOSED GATE — core's principle caught it in code core had never seen (rak4630-fw `ce69273`, 2026-07-17).** core, ruling on the issuer key: *"the natural implementation of an absent env var is SKIP THE CHECK — a fail-open by default, in the gate whose whole job is to fail closed; the failure would be silent and would look exactly like success."* **That is a description of my own v1**: the expected-tg_id binding was an OPTIONAL `env::var` ⇒ **absent var = NO CHECK**. Worse than useless — **it READ like a TG binding existed**, so a reviewer would believe the image was bound when by default it was not. **That is THE SAME MISLABELLING I WAS REPAIRING** (main.rs called a fail-OPEN-on-identity path "FAIL-CLOSED"). **I reproduced the defect's shape INSIDE the fix for the defect.** REMOVED rather than left as false assurance; **both controls re-fired after** (empty-cert 188B ⇒ build FAILS; cert147 336B ⇒ validated). core's reasoning recorded in-file — **the reason outlives the answer**.
> **★ SPECS VINDICATED THE GATE AS CANON-MANDATED, NOT CONSERVATISM — R2-PROVISION:326:** *"Persona present but invalid (corrupt, fails self-consistency, seal/CRC-invalid) → the device MUST fail closed and require a physical reset."* **An empty certificate fails self-consistency** ⇒ my build failure + hard stop are **the MUST we were violating**, not caution we chose. Reframes #72 from "a good idea" to "the rule we were breaking".
> **🛑 #72 DOES *NOT* UNBLOCK THE FLASH (core's picture-correction, and I will not let it blur):** a conformant persona in a **BAKED** image is **still non-conformant** — **R2-PROVISION §5.1 step 3 requires the generic image + Channel-A**, and the RAK bootloader has **ZERO Channel-A implementation**. So **#72 closes the fail-open funnel and NOTHING ELSE**; **the baked path itself is Roy's call.** "Safety fix landed" must not read as "flash unblocked" — that is exactly the **loud-fix-hides-the-silent-hole** shape both core and composer caught me on tonight. Sequencing still stands: #72 is decision-independent.


> **↔ MECHANISM RESOLVED — CORE CONCEDED TO ME, I CONCEDED ITS INVARIANT (2026-07-17; rak4630-fw `0df2c85`).** Two reversals in one exchange, each on evidence:
>   - **core CONCEDED the mechanism: BUILD-INPUT (env path), not a const.** My production argument won: *a dev-trial shortcut becomes the production shape by default unless refused up front; the production issuer is a REAL TG whose pk must not sit in a shared crate.* core, on itself: *"MY OWN DISEASE pointed back at me — a const would have been CURRENTLY fine and STRUCTURALLY wrong. I have spent this night naming currently-true-vs-structurally-true and I proposed the currently-true option."*
>   - **★ core DERIVED composer's claim instead of taking it** — no crypto lib, so it implemented **RFC-8032 pubkey derivation in pure python**, got `tg_pk` from the documented seed, and **matched it against the staged persona's key 5**. That is the difference between accepting evidence and having it. **AND its reading of what it proves is sharper than mine was: composer's argument is about the VALUE's AUDITABILITY, not the MECHANISM** — a seed-derived value is checkable whether it arrives by const or env ⇒ **it never chose build-input; my production argument did.** I had called composer's *"the better half"* — **wrong: different axes, only one load-bearing for the question on the table.**
>   - **✅ CORE'S INVARIANT ADOPTED (non-negotiable, and it survives the mechanism change intact): THE ISSUER PK CHECK IS UNCONDITIONAL — absent anchor = BUILD FAILURE, same loud refusal as the empty cert, NEVER a skipped branch.** core's objection was never the mechanism; it was that *the natural implementation of an absent env var is a skipped branch = a fail-open inside the gate whose entire job is to fail closed.* **Plus core's attribution point I had missed: LOG THE ANCHOR'S SHA — "validated" without naming WHICH issuer it validated against is unattributable; a gate that cannot say what it checked against cannot be audited.**
>   - **⚠ AND CORE'S EXPECTATION-vs-ANCHOR DISTINCTION SHOWS I OVER-CORRECTED — I had DELETED `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID` outright.** core: *an EXPECTATION may be optional; only the ANCHOR may not.* **v1's real defect was not optionality — it was optional AND SILENT** (unset ⇒ no check, while the code READ like a binding existed). **I fixed the lie by removing the capability: the cheap fix, not the right one. RESTORED with the ABSENCE MADE LOUD** — unset now emits *"NO RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID SET — image is NOT bound to any expected trust group; this build will accept a structurally-valid persona for ANY tg_id"*. **THREE controls fired: empty-cert ⇒ FAILS · cert147 ⇒ validated · no-expectation ⇒ ANNOUNCED.**
>   - **★★ THE GENERAL FORM (mine, taken from being wrong twice in one file): MY FIRST INSTINCT ON FINDING A MISLEADING CHECK WAS TO DELETE IT — but the check was never the problem, its SILENCE was. Deleting a misleading signal removes the lie AND the capability together; making it HONEST keeps both halves.** I had been doing exactly this all night in the other direction (naming gaps rather than papering them) and did not apply it to my own code. *An optional check that announces when it is off is honest; one that stays quiet is a lie of omission.*
>   - **NEGATIVE CONTROL CONFIRMED BY CORE'S OWN DERIVATION:** staged repeater `tg_pk = da1aa7f9…` vs rak-persona.bin `tg_pk = 3992f89b…` ⇒ **genuinely different TGs** ⇒ rak-persona.bin is a **negative**-control candidate and **I still have NO positive control**. **(a) lands with composer's cert-bearing persona, both directions fired** — core endorsed the hold rather than pushing me to ship blind.
>   - **ROLE ENFORCEMENT (core's, not mine to duplicate): specs ruled Member `0x02` canon (R2-RUNTIME §3.2.2:246) — the RULING closes the question but NOT the ENFORCEMENT; neither core's parse-hardening nor my gate reads the role byte.** core's framing worth keeping: **it surfaced by auditing the SHADOW of a fix rather than its target.**

> **▶ ESP L2CAP CoC FIX — co-review turn (2026-07-16): answered core's one-per-ACL POLICY Q from metal ground truth; NO edit/push/hardware.**
> Core's ARCH-refined design (fixed command slots not stack-local args; fixed NPL pools BLE_HOST_EV_COUNT=19/SEM_COUNT=10
> → one persistent dispatcher event + bounded app ring + app-level FreeRTOS sem/notify pool; logical channel-generation
> handle not chan*; host-owned registry). My caller-contract UNCHANGED (8 sync-Result send_to sites). Core asked ME (metal-usage
> owner) the one-per-ACL policy Q. **ANSWERED (read-only, verified against canonical `crates/r2-esp/src/l2cap.rs` @ r2-core-consolidation):**
> - **CONFIRM one-per-ACL is R2's real model.** Firmware = PURE CoC SERVER, single PSM 0x00D2 (create_server L171), ZERO
>   connect-out (no `ble_l2cap_connect` anywhere). `send_to` (L185-188) resolves by peer_addr → first non-closing channel; a
>   2nd CoC to the same peer_addr is dead weight send_to never selects. R2 has NO USE for >1 CoC/peer. I back enforce-one-per-ACL fail-closed.
> - **Sharpened the ENFORCEMENT POINT (concrete gap I found):** server-only means we do NOT control how many CoC a REMOTE peer
>   opens on one ACL. `handle_accept` (L398-437) has NO per-conn_handle dedup — accepts a 2nd CoC on the same conn_handle
>   unconditionally. Reject there (non-closing PeerChannel already exists for conn_handle → return error rc) → NimBLE refuses
>   the 2nd channel → core's conn_handle-keyed retain (L460/487) becomes correct-by-construction, aliasing killed at source, not peer-trust.
> - `handle_connected` L460 retain already assumes one-per-conn_handle but SILENTLY evicts a live sibling — same aliasing other side; accept-reject fixes both.
> - Completeness: COC_MAX_NUM=3 is the STACK-WIDE ceiling, NOT per-ACL; one-per-ACL → 3 concurrent peers max; more peers = separate config bump (orthogonal).
> - Sent to core (queued, core busy). STILL GATED: co-review the compile-verified rewrite when core routes it (read-only, allowed); metal validation on Roy hardware GO.

> DISCONNECTED removes EXACT chan+generation = root fix for sibling-aliasing). My earlier "I back one-per-ACL enforcement at handle_accept" is
> SUPERSEDED — generation-per-chan is a strict superset that drops the need for accept-time dedup. My sync-Result send_to caller-contract + 8 sites

So D4.hk == RAK.hk == XIAO.hk, measured on both sides. The sealed JoinResponse shows NO match — **EXPECTED, not a mismatch**: it is an X25519/XChaCha20 EncryptedJoinResponse (R2-TRUST §5.2), 252B = 24 nonce + 212 ct + 16 tag (I verified the size exactly), so a raw-byte scan CANNOT see the hk by construction. composer's ATTESTATION: minter.rs:11/162 — the persona bundle is the §3.2 JoinResponse SUPERSET, ONE code path writes tg.hk into BOTH.
> - **⚠ I SHARPENED composer's 'closed-by-construction' — it is CONDITIONAL, and I named the condition.** One code path proves the same FIELD SOURCE, **not the same tg VALUE at two mint times** — and the artifacts **span a run boundary**: rak-persona 07-14 08:34, d4 07-14 18:45, xiao 07-14 18:46, **JoinResponse 07-15 06:27 (~12h later)**. Identical code + a different wallet tg entry = identical structure, different hk. **CORROBORATION I FOUND FOR THEM (they hadn't cited it):** the three personas were minted in SEPARATE runs across ~10 HOURS and ALL carry the SAME hk fingerprint => composer's wallet tg entry was EMPIRICALLY STABLE across multiple runs, making stability across the further 12h likely — **likely, not measured**. **LAST LINK = android fingerprinting the hk it recovers AFTER decrypting the JoinResponse** (needs the device mesh_sk; composer by design does not hold it). Until then: artifact chain (solid) + measured persona hk-equality (solid) + structural attestation (strong) + **measured end-to-end (PENDING)**. I will NOT call it proven.

(likely: attest at MINT time by recording the digest, not by re-opening later).

> - **✅ CORE CO-REVIEWED `ef6f95a` = PASS + "FROM MY SIDE THE CHAIN IS READY: GO TO METAL" (core state db61e4e, branch-only, 867 tests / 0 failed; RAK thumbv7em; nrf54-lr2021 thumbv8m). I RAN CORE'S PROOF INSTEAD OF BANKING IT — verdict CONFIRMED, proof UNSOUND.** Core replaced my call-site COUNT with an EGRESS-CLOSURE proof (strictly better method: a count of 6 can't prove there's no 7th). **But core enumerated a PROXY for the boundary, not the boundary:**
>   - **CRACK 1 — core's premise "DATA_TX_LORA is the ONLY way onto the LoRa carrier" is FALSE.** The real carrier edge is `lora.send`, and it has **TWO** sites: main.rs:5043 (the DATA_TX_LORA drain core enumerated) **and main.rs:5055 — `build_lora_beacon` → `lora.send`, bypassing DATA_TX_LORA entirely**, inside `lora_route_task` (cfg `loraroute`) ⇒ **it IS in the demo image.** Core enumerated a QUEUE that FEEDS the edge. **Core's conclusion survives via an argument core never made:** the missed sender emits a §8.1 discovery beacon (magic 0xB2, ver 0x01, ≤17B) built by DIRECT byte-assembly at main.rs:4684 — it never touches `encode_extended`, so it cannot carry an extended frame.
>   - **CRACK 2 — core's "xiao_bridge_task:5419 is compact BY CONSTRUCTION, phone-originated" is FALSE.** It is an **UNVALIDATED OPAQUE PASSTHROUGH**: `copy_from_slice(&inbuf[3..3+bl])` → `try_send`, **no decode, no format check**. The 2 `decode_compact` calls in that task are the OPPOSITE direction (LoRa→USB egress; its own comment: *"the phone does the authoritative verify_compact"*). A host tagging an **extended** frame with `LORA_LOCAL_ID` gets it radiated verbatim. Compact by **HOST CONVENTION**, not construction.
>   - **SCOPE, HONESTLY — crack 2 does NOT touch the demo, twice over:** (i) 5419 is `cfg(feature="xiaobridge")`; the demo compose is `fakesensor,benchsf7,dev,baked_persona` and `fakesensor = [otaengine, loraroute, loratcxo]` ⇒ xiaobridge NOT pulled ⇒ **task compiled OUT**; (ii) independently, 5419 is the **phone→LoRa** direction while the demo data path is sensor→LoRa→bridge→phone — **the opposite way**. Real property of the *xiaobridge* image; **tracked, NOT patched before Roy's slot.**
>   - **★ THE PROOF THAT ACTUALLY HOLDS (demo image, by construction):** `lora.send` = exactly 2 sites, both in `lora_route_task`. **5043** ← DATA_TX_LORA ← senders: `mesh_broadcast:4199` (sole caller **6143**, traced to `encode_compact`) + `xiao_bridge_task:5419` (compiled out under fakesensor). **5055** ← `build_lora_beacon` (direct assembly, never `encode_extended`). ⇒ **every byte reaching the LoRa carrier in the demo image is either `encode_compact` or a §8.1 beacon. No extended, by construction — closed over the REAL edge.** ⇒ **VERDICT UNCHANGED: GO TO METAL.**
>   - **★★ THE RULE (banked in [[never-conclude-from-a-null]]): CLOSE OVER THE ACTUAL BOUNDARY, NOT A PROXY FOR IT.** *"Enumerate everything that reaches X"* is a proof only when X is the real edge. Ask **"what is the LAST thing before the air/disk/socket?"** and enumerate THAT — a queue/channel/wrapper is an *implementation* of the edge and there can be a second one. **Dangerous because it is proof-SHAPED, so it disarms review**; its null ("no other senders") reads as a theorem when the method could never see the bypass. **Positive control: grep the PRIMITIVE and check your enumeration already contains every hit.** You pick the proxy because it's where the DESIGN says data flows — **but the bypass never read the design.**
>   - **HONEST SYMMETRY:** core was right that my count couldn't prove there was no 7th site — there were in fact **EIGHT** `encode_extended` sites, not 6 (**1783** + **5949**), and **both go to `socket.send_to` (UDP/WiFi), where extended is canon-legal**. So my count was wrong **AND harmless**, exactly as core's method predicts. **Core's METHOD beat mine; my EXECUTION beat core's. Keep both halves.**
> - **✅✅ CORE CONCEDED ALL THREE + SHARPENED THE RULE — then its CONCESSION carried a 4th UNVERIFIED claim that SOFTENED my finding. I tested it. FALSE. (core state db61e4e..46528e3, 867 tests / 0 failed, nothing pushed. VERDICT: GO TO METAL, unchanged, now for the right reason.)**
>   - **CORE'S OWN NAMING OF ITS ERROR (better than my polite version):** *"I took a CODE COMMENT as a construction proof."* :5419's comment says "TX the compact body on-air"; core read that **prose** and wrote "compact by construction". *"That is strictly worse than your call-site count: you at least enumerated real code and got a wrong-but-harmless answer; I enumerated prose."*
>   - **★★ THE RULE, IN ITS FINAL FORM (core's sharpening of my diagnosis — keep this one):** *"You picked the queue because the queue is where the DESIGN says frames go — but the beacon never read the design."* ⇒ **a proxy-closure only covers the paths that OBEY the architecture, so it is exactly blind to the bypass — and a bypass is the only thing a closure proof exists to catch. THE PROXY IS CHOSEN BY READING THE DESIGN; THE VIOLATION IS DEFINED BY NOT READING IT.** So **"close over the boundary"** and **"the design cannot be the search index"** are the SAME rule. **Generalises past LoRa: any "all writes go through the repository / logger / queue / API" argument is a proxy-closure until someone enumerates the syscall.** Sits beside the day's other two — *state the SCOPE with the result* (a null needs a positive control) and *close over the EDGE* (a closure needs the real boundary): **both are one disease — a confident green over the wrong universe.**
>   - **★ MY REFUTATION OF CORE'S MITIGATION — the finding is SHARPER than core's own sharpening.** Core softened it: *"the host is paired (r2-usb-pair), so this is not a stranger-on-the-wire — but trusted host is an authorisation argument, not a conformance one."* Right about the KIND of argument; **WRONG on the fact. PAIRING DOES NOT GATE THE LoRa TX PRIMITIVE** (VERIFIED main.rs:5410-5419): the demux has **three SIBLING branches** — `looks_control(0xFF)` → `pairing.handle` → `persist_link_key`; `!synced && looks_sync` → consume SYNC; **`plen>1 && inbuf[2]==LORA_LOCAL_ID` → `copy_from_slice` → `DATA_TX_LORA.try_send`**. The third checks **NO** pairing state, **NO** link_key, and does **NOT** require `synced` — **it SETS `synced=true`**. `persisted_link_key` is loaded (:5220) and handed to `Peripheral::new` (:5228), then **NEVER consulted on the TX path** (grep positive-controlled: 11 `pairing` hits ⇒ the null is real; link_key touches = :299/:304 load, :2726/:2742 flash record, :5399/:5406-7 inside the pairing branch — **none gate the radiate**). ⇒ **an UNPAIRED host, with NO SYNC, that never ran the SM, can radiate.** The pairing SM runs **ALONGSIDE** the primitive, not **IN FRONT OF** it ⇒ **it provides ZERO protection here.** The only real bound is **PHYSICAL USB ACCESS** — the same bound with or without pairing. **So: not "a paired host can radiate any bytes" — "ANY host that can reach the port can radiate any bytes."** Both of core's axes survive; the authorisation axis no longer softens it.
>   - **★★ NEW COROLLARY (banked in [[never-conclude-from-a-null]]): WE AUDIT *ESCALATIONS* HARDER THAN *DE-ESCALATIONS*, SO DE-ESCALATIONS ARE WHERE UNVERIFIED CLAIMS SURVIVE.** Core's concession was rigorous on the 3 refuted claims and then added a 4th, unverified, that made the finding smaller. **Not motivated — the same reflex as "compact by construction": a plausible fact read off the DESIGN instead of the code.** The SM *is* there, *is* wired, *looks* like it guards the port. **A softening claim needs the SAME positive control as a hardening one, and gets LESS scrutiny precisely because it lowers the stakes.** ⇒ **Applies to MY OWN de-escalations** ("only cosmetic", "compiled out", "not on the demo path") — each is a claim; scope-verify it as hard as an alarm.
>   - **THE PROPERTY, STATED PLAINLY (core asked for it harder than "a xiaobridge quirk", and it's right): the xiaobridge image will RADIATE VERBATIM ANY BYTES the USB host tags with `LORA_LOCAL_ID`.** Not "may carry extended" — **ANY bytes.** An **arbitrary-LoRa-transmit primitive exposed to the host**, whose conformance consequence is that the image can violate **R2-LORA §5.1** at the host's discretion **with no code in the DFR disagreeing.** **Tracked: hive task #69. NOT patched before Roy's slot** (flashed image in the proven anchor path ⇒ unpriced risk, zero demo benefit).

>   - **★★ MY CHALLENGE 1 — "THE DFR IS NON-CONFORMANT TODAY" OVERSTATES IT, and the distinction IS the spec gap.** §5.1's MUST NOT binds **BEHAVIOUR**. Accurate: **CONFORMANT IN BEHAVIOUR but UNENFORCING**, its conformance **CONTINGENT ON THE HOST** rather than guaranteed. ⇒ **THE REAL QUESTION: does a MUST NOT bind only BEHAVIOUR, or also require an ENFORCEMENT POINT at the last node that can still stop it?** Canon does not say — **that ambiguity IS the gap**. It prices the fix: *"non-conformant today"* = shipping a violation (urgent); *"unenforced"* = a defence + a text fix (not urgent). **Specs is right about the FIX and wrong about the LABEL.**

The floor-steelman (extended ≥54 B always) dies on canon's **own rows**: `:377` *"These rows are COMPACT-format sizes"*, **SF7 = 51 B→103 ms, 115 B→195 ms, 222 B→348 ms**; a 54 B extended frame at SF7 ≈ **110 ms**. ⇒ **canon TABULATES compact frames at SF7 costing 195 ms and 348 ms as legitimate operating points — 2× and 3× the airtime of the extended frame it FORBIDS.** A ToA rationale would ban 54 B extended while blessing 222 B compact at 3× the cost. **No coherent rule does that.** ⇒ **§5.1 states EXACTLY ONE ground (MTU); the paragraph never mentions airtime. MY CLAIM STANDS UNQUALIFIED: on SF7 the justification is not half dead — it is dead.** *What survives of their instinct:* extended costs **+24 B for the same content** (32 B vs 8 B HMAC) — the apiary 29 B/67 ms reading → ~53 B/~105 ms, ~1.6× airtime, marginally busting 1/s@10%. **A real efficiency reason to prefer compact; NOT the ground of a MUST NOT.** *Free nit:* `:401`'s takeaway overstates its own table — **SF7/51 B = 103 ms = 0.97/s**, already missing both 1/s and 100 ms. ⇒ asked specs to **DROP/RECAST their proposed 3rd defect**; the real one is *"canon states a rationale that DOES NOT BIND on the bench profile canon itself blesses (`:386` labelled WHOLE-MESH SF7/BW125)"*.

So it **never assents to extended** ⇒ satisfies specs' first horn (*"either never negotiates extended"*) — **BY ACCIDENT, NOT BY CONSTRUCTION.** **Ignoring a negotiation ≠ refusing one:** a host that sends extended **without** negotiating still gets it radiated. ⇒ **specs' two horns are NOT EXHAUSTIVE for a real implementation — there is a THIRD state, NEGOTIATION-IGNORING: conformant on the handshake, unenforcing on the air.** Flagged for §3.3.

Bridge domain = *"any framed bytes the host sends"* (**that IS its function**, per `R2-USB:32` — the host is not a foreign party but the same organism) ⇒ extended is **inside** it ⇒ **non-conformant, no malice or mistake required**. io_task's domain **excludes** *"an extended frame to radiate"* — reaching it requires **EDITING THE BUILD, not supplying an input** ⇒ **conformant**. Keeps the teeth, drops the over-reach, **and is TESTABLE**. ⇒ **It is the egress-closure rule pointed at the ingress: for ENFORCEMENT close over the EGRESS (cannot be outflanked); for CONFORMANCE close over the INPUT DOMAIN.**

> - **✅✅ CORE'S §5.1 ESCAPE-HATCH UNSOUNDNESS — VERIFIED, AND §5.1'S *OWN CITED AUTHORITY* CONVICTS IT.** Core's argument: MTU was never the real obstacle — compact/extended aren't self-describing, so a receiver **MIS-PARSES** the wrong tier rather than rejecting it; **raising the MTU creates NO discriminator**, so the hatch licenses exactly the failure the rule exists to prevent. **CONFIRMED FROM SOURCE, and the spec convicts itself:** §5.1:326 cites *"R2-WIRE §4.3.5 **format-detection**"* as though a discriminator existed. **`R2-WIRE.md:453`, verbatim: *"A receiving hive distinguishes compact from extended format **BY TRANSPORT CONTEXT**: messages received on BLE or LoRa adapters are parsed as compact."*** ⇒ **IT DETECTS NOTHING — IT ASSUMES.** The section named *Format Detection* hard-codes format per bearer, so **a LoRa receiver parses everything as compact BY SPEC** ⇒ an extended frame on LoRa isn't rejected, it's **mis-parsed**. Core was right and didn't need me to be.
>   - **★★ MY STRENGTHENING — THE HATCH IS NOT A PHY DECISION, IT IS A BREAKING WIRE CHANGE.** If Roy gated the SF9/115 B profile, **§4.3.5:453 would STILL mandate "messages received on LoRa adapters are parsed as compact"** ⇒ **every conformant receiver on that profile mis-parses the very extended frames the profile exists to carry.** So the hatch needs a **THREE-way change**: an in-band **discriminator (a wire change)** + amend **§4.3.5** + amend **§5.1**. **It READS like "Roy approves a PHY profile" and MEANS "break the wire format."** ⇒ **THE HATCH UNDERSTATES ITS OWN COST BY AN ORDER OF MAGNITUDE** — a stronger reason to kill it than inconsistency: it's **mispriced in a way that invites someone to grant it cheaply.**
>   - **★ NEW — THE DEAD MTU RATIONALE IS *DUPLICATED*, so fixing §5.1 alone leaves the corpse in R2-WIRE.** `§4.3.5:463`: *"On LoRa this is moot: the LoRa bearer is compact-only (R2-LORA §5.1), and a signed extended frame cannot even fit the SF12/BW125 MTU (54-byte floor > 51, R2-LORA §5.2)."* **Same MTU argument, same SF12 scoping, same death on SF7.**
>   - **★ NEW — §4.3.5 HAS §5.1'S EXACT SHAPE: an absolute rule + an unacknowledged escape whose mechanism DOESN'T EXIST.** `:453` states detection-by-transport-context **absolutely**; `:463` then says a signed frame is *"forwarded VERBATIM… the receiver parses it by the **carried format context**, not by transport default"* — an exception `:453` never admits — **and canon concedes the mechanism is undefined on that same line: *"a format-context surface to COORDINATE WITH CORE."*** ⇒ **the exception invokes something that does not exist, and it is CORE's crate that would have to invent it. Two specs, one pattern.** Core has routed the re-grounding to specs: **base the MUST NOT on SINGLE-TIER-PER-BEARER** (no in-band discriminator ⇒ mixed tiers structurally undecodable ⇒ **binds on EVERY profile**), demote MTU to a **coincidental SF12-only enforcer**, and **KILL the hatch** (extended-on-LoRa would need a **discriminator = a wire change, not airtime**).

>   - **✅ I CONFIRMED THE MECHANISM AGAINST THE RAK ARTIFACT (not reasoned):** the RAK feeds EVERY raw RxDone buffer into `handle_rx_frame` with **NO beacon pre-demux** (rak4630 main.rs:954); `handle_rx_frame` step (1) is `decode_extended` and **decode-fail `return no` BEFORE any neighbour formation** (r2-dataplane lib.rs:516-519); **a beacon fails that decode ⇒ forms NO link.** ⇒ **only decodable DATA frames populate the RAK's neighbour table.** In the minimal READ demo the XIAO emits only §8.1 BEACONS on LoRa and the phone transmits nothing ⇒ **the RAK hears exactly ONE data source, D4 the sender** ⇒ table = {sender} ⇒ F2 empties the plan ⇒ dead relay leg. **The phone sees only the direct D4→XIAO path (route_len=1) at 30cm — indistinguishable from success.**
>   - **★ THE FLIP IS *TOPOLOGY*, NOT COMPOSE:** if ANY hive other than D4 transmits a **decodable LoRa DATA** frame the RAK hears (2nd LoRa node #66, or D2 on-air on LoRa), F2's exclusion leaves a viable neighbour ⇒ relay alive. So the member compose is dead **IFF the RAK hears only D4** — non-deterministic if a 2nd transmitter is intermittent (**two runs of the same demo can differ** — worse than deterministic failure). **PIN THE TOPOLOGY, not just the compose.**

>   - **★★ THEIR SPEC ARGUMENT UNDERSTATES ITSELF.** Core: *"canon knows how to do in-band demux, it just NEVER GAVE compact/extended one."* **VERIFIED SHARPER — canon GAVE them one and SPENT IT ON THE SAME VALUE TWICE:** `compact.rs:54` and `extended.rs:50` are **THE SAME CALL** — `buf[0] = encode_byte0(h.version, h.msg_type, h.flags)`. `decode_byte0` rejects `ver != 0` ⇒ **3 of 4 version values (1,2,3) UNUSED.** And **the beacon demux works PRECISELY BECAUSE the beacon uses ver=2** — it is discriminable **by the very field the two tiers left identical.** ⇒ **THE DISCRIMINATOR IS PRESENT, 2 BITS WIDE, 3 OF 4 VALUES FREE, AND BOTH TIERS WERE ASSIGNED ver=0.** `§4.3.5:453`'s *"detection by transport context"* is a workaround for a **SOLVED** problem left unsolved in one place.
>   - **★★★ ⇒ THIS REFUTES CORE'S RE-GROUNDING AS WORDED.** *"No in-band discriminator ⇒ mixed tiers are **STRUCTURALLY** undecodable — binds on EVERY profile"* is **FALSE.** They are undecodable **BY CHOICE**, one spent value away from decodable. **Same over-claim shape as core's other four** (prose-as-proof → proxy-as-boundary → architecture-as-mitigation → proxy-as-boundary-in-a-type → **structural-from-current-state**) — *"count is now five, one shape"* — **and this one would have gone into CANON.** ⇒ **A rule needs a ground that is TRUE, not merely CURRENTLY TRUE**: a re-grounding on "structurally impossible" gets refuted **the day someone reads `types.rs`**, and then the MUST NOT has lost its **SECOND** ground in a week (the MTU one is already dead on benchsf7).
>   - **THE HONEST GROUND (still core's): mixed tiers are undecodable BECAUSE BOTH FORMATS WERE ASSIGNED ver=0** — contingent, fixable, **and the fix converts a MIS-PARSE into a clean `Err`**, which is the property core actually cares about: **today** an extended frame on LoRa **passes** `decode_byte0` (ver=0 ✓) then garbages; **at ver=1, TODAY'S UNMODIFIED DECODER returns `InvalidVersion` — it FAILS CLOSED.** ⚠ **I did NOT prescribe ver=1** — core's crate, and the cost is real: `version` is a **protocol version**, so tier-tagging it spends version space (2 bits = 4 values) and makes tier×version a product; a free **flag bit** may be better (`b & 0x07`) — **unverified, and not mine to design.** **My only claim: "structurally undecodable" is NOT AVAILABLE AS A PREMISE.**

> - **★★ CORE'S GENERALISATION — the most valuable output of the day, and bigger than LoRa: "A PHYSICAL LIMIT IS NOT A CONFORMANCE CHECK — it only HIDES the violation on the profile where the limit binds."** Review question for specs: **WHICH OF OUR MUSTs ARE ONLY "ENFORCED" BY A LIMIT SOME FUTURE PROFILE REMOVES?** Wherever a spec MUST coincides with a physical constraint, **the MUST is UNTESTED** — and the day someone widens the constraint (a bench profile, a faster PHY, a bigger MTU) the violation ships silently. **MY COROLLARY:** the constraint is often removed by the SAFEST-LOOKING change — `benchsf7` exists purely to make the demo fast, and it is what unmasked a 7-day-old canon violation. **A convenience knob removed an accidental safety property nobody knew they were relying on.** Routed to specs.

> - **★ WHY IT'S LIVE ON THE BENCH BUT INVISIBLE IN THE FIELD (core's catch, and it's sharp):** a SIGNED extended frame is 22B hdr + 32B HMAC = **54B floor > the 51B SF12/BW125 control-profile MTU**, and §5.2 rejects over-MTU **with no fragmentation** => on the FIELD SF12 profile a signed extended frame is **physically un-transmittable** and the bug can never show. **The demo runs benchsf7 (SF7/BW125 = 222B MTU) — which is EXACTLY what makes the non-conformant leg emittable. The bench profile is the unmasker.** My io_task LoRa emissions are a MIX: **4 signed** (sign_extended -> encode_extended -> mesh_broadcast) + **2 forward/relay re-encodes**. HAZARD (why it's worse than a dropped frame): a Compact-mode RAK does NOT cleanly Err on extended — extended byte0 is structurally decodable (same ver|type|flags packing) => decode_compact MIS-PARSES it, and with core's #2 (any heard frame forms a LINK) it would form a neighbour under a **GARBAGE hive_id**, then relay-opaque re-broadcast garbage (TTL/dedup-bounded, but pollutes the table + burns airtime). There is NO reliable in-band discriminator — which is precisely WHY canon makes the bearer single-tier.

Both vectors exist => no rework for android/composer either way. Routed to supervisor for Roy.

> - **SECOND decode-consistency check (android relocated the +1-shift risk correctly): core-ffi USB decode.** android's Kotlin hands raw USB bytes to core-ffi feed() (owns SYNC/compact-reassembly/HMAC -> FfiDecodedFrame); android's ApiaryReading.decode() runs on the already-extracted 6 BE payload = shift-immune. So the 0x02-strip + compact-decode live in core-ffi. > **▶ RE-PASS ROUND 2 (2026-07-16) — hive-codex read-only re-pass of the amended commit returned 3 findings; all triaged, NO PUSH.**
> - **F1 (HIGH, CI blocker) — first fix was itself fail-OPEN; SUPERSEDED by round 4 (see below).** The
>   `m=$(grep … | … | sort)` substitutions abort the docs step under Actions' `bash -e -o pipefail` when a
>   grep matches NOTHING (clean) or all matches are allowlisted. My round-2 fix wrapped the WHOLE pipeline in
>   `|| true` — which ALSO swallowed a scanner CRASH (rc>1: bad pattern, missing grep) and mapped it to a clean
>   result. hive-codex round-4 caught that as a NEW fail-open. Correct fix is in round 4: a `scan()` helper that
>   treats grep rc 0/1 as success but PROPAGATES rc>1 (fail-closed), with `|| true` on ONLY the allowlist filter.
> - **F3 (MED, test weakness) — DONE.** `kat()` now accepts optional `reason` ([MAC]/[TAIL]/[TAIL-0x]/[TAIL-COMPACT]) and exact `count`; high-value KATs assert them so a wrong-CLASSIFIER regression (MAC misread as TAIL, or the 4-group run's 2-window count) can no longer stay green on a bare flag/no-flag check. Selftest **41/41** with the stricter asserts.
> - **F2 (MED, false-positives) — VERIFIED, one sub-claim REFUTED, narrowing DEFERRED as a Roy-canon tradeoff.**
>   (Examples described abstractly here on purpose — writing the literal token beside a context word would trip
>   this very gate on RESUME.md; see the self-inflicted-trap note in memory.) Confirmed latent FPs, all currently
>   ABSENT from the tree: a time-of-day triple or a short two-digit-group date sitting beside a board/device word
>   classifies as a TAIL; a six-digit baud constant beside a board-id label classifies as a compact tail; a
>   revision-like six-hex filename segment can too. REFUTED: ISO-date *filenames* with a four-digit year do NOT
>   flag — the hex negative-lookbehind already blocks them (the year's last digit is hex before the date run).
>   Decision: the gate is fail-SAFE by design (errs toward flagging, exact-allowlist escape hatch); every F2 fix
>   narrows CONTEXT = the fail-OPEN direction that burned this workstream twice, and the real tree is currently
>   clean (exit 0). Not narrowing unilaterally; routed to hive-codex/supervisor as a noise-vs-fail-open tradeoff on
>   Roy-canon context rules. **Do-not-assume:** narrowing the tail-context set to quiet F2 without KATs proving no
>   new fail-open is the exact regression class this branch exists to kill.
>
> **▶ RE-PASS ROUND 3 (2026-07-16) — hive-codex found a real fail-open I had wrongly claimed closed; FIXED + F4 routed. NO PUSH.**
> - **MIXED-SEPARATOR bypass (HIGH, fail-open) — FIXED.** The classifier SKIPPED any pair-run containing both
>   separator characters (`next if token has both ':' and '-'`), so a 6-pair MAC written with mixed separators
>   emitted NOTHING. My round-2 re-pass message CLAIMED "colon+hyphen+mixed all normalize" — that was FALSE; the
>   code skipped mixed. hive-codex caught the overclaim. Fix = drop the skip, normalise both separators to one
>   before classifying, so colon/hyphen/mixed now genuinely all normalise. Flipped the KAT that encoded the old
>   skip (was must-PASS → now must-FLAG) and added mixed-separator positives incl. an end-to-end production-
>   extraction case. Selftest **43/43**; full gate over the real tree still clean (exit 0) → flagging mixed adds
>   NO false positive. **Do-not-assume:** don't re-introduce a "malformed = skip" arm; a leak gate errs toward flagging.

> **▶ RE-PASS ROUND 4 (2026-07-16) — hive-codex refuted my OWN round-2/3 fixes; both were real. FIXED. NO PUSH.**
> - **docs F1 fail-OPEN (HIGH) — properly FIXED.** The round-2 blanket `|| true` mapped a scanner CRASH (grep
>   rc>1: missing binary, invalid pattern, unreadable tree) to the same empty/clean result as a legit no-match —
>   fail-open. Replaced with a `scan()` helper: grep rc 0/1 = success (emit matches, empty on no-match), rc>1
>   PROPAGATES so `set -e` aborts = fail-CLOSED; `|| true` now wraps ONLY the allowlist filter (its rc1 = all
>   placeholders, never a tool failure). Verified end-to-end incl. the decisive case: a broken grep (rc2) now
>   makes the step EXIT 2 (fail-closed), not exit-0-clean. Clean→0, planted MAC→1, allowlisted-only→0 all hold.
> - **kat() crash-suppression (MED) — FIXED.** `kat()` used `hygiene_scan || true`, so a scanner crash on a
>   VALID must-pass fixture false-passed. Now captures the scanner status (`&& src=0 || src=$?`) and FAILs the
>   KAT on any non-zero on valid input; the malformed-stream crash path is checked separately. Proved with an
>   injected `hygiene_scan(){ return 3; }` — kat() reports FAIL (old code printed ok). Selftest **43/43**.
> - **merge-legitimate-fragments precision (noise, NOT fail-open) — documented tradeoff.** A timestamp+segment
>   like a time triple joined by a separator to another triple normalises to six pairs and flags [MAC]; spaced
>   fragments pass. Inherently ambiguous; under the fail-SAFE policy this is a noise tradeoff, not a hole. Policy:
>   keep flagging (fail-safe); if a real doc trips it, use a `T`/space separator or an exact allowlist entry.
>
> **▶ RE-PASS ROUND 5 (2026-07-16) — hive-codex found my round-4 fix STILL had two fail-opens. FIXED. NO PUSH.**
> - **docs allowlist filter fail-OPEN (HIGH) — FIXED.** Round 4 fixed the primary `scan()` grep but left the
>   allowlist step as `{ grep -vixE … || true; }`. That `|| true` ALSO swallowed a filter tool failure (rc>1): if
>   the allowlist grep errored while upstream emitted a REAL MAC, the leak was erased and the pipeline read clean.
>   Reproduced. Fixed with an `allow_filter` helper (same rc discipline as `scan`): rc0/1 = success, rc>1 propagates
>   = fail-CLOSED. Verified: allowlist-grep rc2 + upstream real MAC now EXITS NONZERO, not clean.
> - **end-to-end KATs discarded exit status (MED) — FIXED.** The `hygiene_scan_tree` KATs used `[ -n "$(…)" ]` /
>   `[ -z … ]`, which drop the command-substitution status, so a scanner crash that emitted a finding (or emitted
>   nothing) false-passed. Replaced with an `e2e MODE NAME` helper that captures output AND status separately:
>   flag = findings+rc0, clean = empty+rc0, failclosed = rc≠0. The empty-tree KAT is the one explicit rc≠0 case.
> - RESUME durable line corrected (no longer claims blanket `|| true`); strongest temp-repo mixed-EUI/mixed-separator
>   replay recorded PASS (both mixed orders + mixed EUI-64 + underscore/-if00 path form all flag [MAC] end-to-end;
>   allowlisted placeholder passes). F4/Pages branch stays HELD (supervisor-codex: publication policy, not a hygiene
>   fix). Writer ownership RESOLVED: resident hive lane is sole r2-hive writer (Roy/supervisor final).

>   sibling check's `|| true` / bare `if assignment` is the identical hole. Fail-CLOSED must hold gate-wide.

## 🔬 XIAO BENCH decode-support (android, 2026-07-12) — golden frames handed + board-health cleared (commit 95d5148)
android hit two things decoding the XIAO USB egress: (1) InvalidRouteLen on live captures, (2) the stream went QUIET.
**Both answered via fleet send + persisted to docs/BENCH-BOARD-FACTS.md.** (1) ROOT CAUSE = capture drop, NOT a
decoder bug: `dd bs=1` byte-drops the egress (27–30B vs true fixed 31B); byte0=0x06 sets has_route, so ONE dropped
byte reads data[12] as rlen=0x00 = InvalidRouteLen exactly. Handed a byte-exact GOLDEN frame from canonical
`r2_wire::encode_compact` (round-trips decode_compact): compact 31B = `0653000164cedbf305fe0701011234a10018eaa101182a0102030405060708`;
R2-USB DATA record 33B = `1f00…` (1f00 = payload_len 31 LE). Emitter LANDED = `crates/r2-hive-bin/examples/gen_golden_compact_frame.rs`
(regen: `cargo run -p r2-hive --example gen_golden_compact_frame`). 0xA1 sighting golden already byte-exact in
dfr1195 `USB-BEACON-SIGHTING-FORMAT.md` KAT. (2) QUIET = peer-silence (egress is PURE forwarded LoRa RX, NO
keepalive); board still enumerated at same MAC = NOT in ROM download mode; forward-task can't wedge on a DTR toggle
(USB-JTAG egress drops-when-unread, never blocks). Did NOT touch the board.
**★ BEARER-OWNER DECISIONS LOCKED (composer eb0bc75 + android, 2026-07-12):** LoRa REAL + WiFi REAL + BLE dark.
**(a) fw inject-per-transport harness CANCELLED** (composer #2 — no no-RF sim leg needed; removed from open items).
**(b) NEW hive task #66 (composer #1), GATED on supervisor GO:** stand a 2nd LoRa node at SF7 (`benchsf7`) as the
R2-PROVISION §3.2 JOIN counterparty to the XIAO (android is phone-provisioner ONLY). Deps on GO: 2nd SX1262 board
attached (RAK DISCONNECTED — need Roy hw) + a JOIN-role build (not keyless xiaobridge). **BLE-REAL FINALIZED (composer 0b2d0bd)** — not skip. Reflash `xiaobridge,ble` still HELD but ADDITIVE (keeps LoRa
bridge + adds ble_task); trigger = AFTER (a) WiFi leg proven AND (b) android BlueZ central built, at a convenient
break in android's live capture. **✅ compile-verified locally (xtensa esp toolchain): `xiaobridge,ble,benchsf7`
builds GREEN (warnings-only) = no feature-unification blocker.** **⚠ compile-green ≠ coex-proven** — BLE+WiFi+LoRa on

**★★★ 2026-07-13 — cad8b57 HELD (hive-codex CRITICAL, correctly caught); SUPERSEDE with a redesigned local successor (GO, compile-only, no push/flash until twin-clean).** cad8b57 (bootloader gate) + ec29da4 (re-vendor) = LOCAL commits, UNPUSHED. C2 reject ignores STATE-erase failure → erased bytes copied into ACTIVE. **CORRECTED MAP (successor):** BOOTLOADER 0x0-0x20000 | STATE 0x20000-0x21000 (4K, proven) | OTA-META 0x21000-0x22000 (candidate prefix+approval) | PERSONA 0x22000-0x24000 | ACTIVE 0x24000-0x91000 (436K/109pg) | DFU 0x91000-0xFF000 (440K/110pg = ACTIVE+1, the documented min) | JOURNAL 0xFF000-0x100000 (4K confirmed-floor, OUTSIDE the swap). **SUCCESSOR REQUIREMENTS (GO):** (1) ONE shared geometry source (app+boot+ota.rs+persona) + build-time overlap/boundary KATs. (2) ALWAYS-VERIFY, gated on embassy-boot's OWN progress counter — NO separate approval record/digest (supervisor Occam+security refutation 2026-07-13, VERIFIED vs embassy-boot-0.7.0 source). Why the digest was dropped: (a) the payload-SHA256 (the expensive part) is paid EITHER WAY (verify checks payload_hash; skip recomputes the digest over the same bytes) — skip saves ONLY the Ed25519 (~tens of ms) ONCE PER OTA (fresh swap), not per boot (normal State::Boot = zero crypto); (b) the digest adds ZERO security — a flash-writing attacker forges the skip in BOTH models (writes record = SHA256(their header‖sig‖payload); bootloader recomputes over their DFU, matches, skips), identical to forging the progress counter; both rely SOLELY on H4 ACL flash-lock. Ground truth (boot_loader.rs): read_state()==Swap for BOTH fresh & in-progress (magic-only); swap() physically ROTATES DFU↔ACTIVE pages, so mid-swap the DFU payload is scrambled/unverifiable; at current_progress()==0 NOTHING is written yet (first op touches only the DFU scratch page at progress→1; first DFU-payload overwrite not until progress≥2) ⇒ progress==0 is a HARD pristine-DFU guarantee. Gate: State::Swap && progress==0 ⇒ FRESH ⇒ read header+sig from OTA-META + stream pristine DFU payload ⇒ full verify_staged_slot (Ed25519 + SHA256==payload_hash + seq>floor) ⇒ PASS → call prepare_boot (starts swap); FAIL → checked-reject. State::Swap && progress>0 ⇒ swap already begun (scrambled) ⇒ NEVER verify, NEVER reject/erase ⇒ pass straight to prepare_boot (embassy resumes). Power-cut in the verify→prepare window leaves progress==0 ⇒ next boot re-verifies pristine DFU (idempotent). The durable "already-authorized" signal is embassy-boot's progress counter itself — no record to write/bind. NOTE: this reads STATE progress words directly (magic@0, valid-marker@WRITE_SIZE, progress@2·WRITE_SIZE+, per embassy-boot 0.7/0.12) — KAT-pin this layout + re-verify on any embassy-boot bump. (3) checked reject — prove STATE non-SWAP (readback) before DFU erase, else fail-stop. (4) payload gate — 0<len≤ACTIVE_LEN, PT_FIRMWARE_FULL, bootable-vector sanity, USE VerifiedUpdate. (5) split dev-bench vs prod DeviceContext (prod = persona/board/device/battery, fail-closed if unavailable). (6) confirmed floor in the SEPARATE atomic JOURNAL page + pending/confirm lifecycle, NO floor=0 fallback. (7) H4 BPROT/ACL — NOT a permitted follow-up for a prod-compilable successor (coordinator correction 2026-07-13): the PROD bootloader build MUST apply reset-time BPROT/ACL protecting BOOTLOADER (0x0-0x20000) + PERSONA (0x22000-0x24000) so a compromised app cannot rewrite the anchor/bootloader, AND partition-wrap the app's Nvmc writes to its own regions; the ONLY unprotected build is an EXPLICITLY-NAMED dev/bench feature; a prod build without protection MUST fail-closed at COMPILE time (compile_error!/const-assert), never silently ship unprotected. Implemented WITH increment 2 (bootloader). ★ ACCEPTANCE (exact re-pass, coordinator 2026-07-13): there must be NO production path that boots with a WRITABLE bootloader/persona — every prod build either boots ACL-protected or does not compile; only the explicit dev/bench feature boots unprotected. (8) falsifiers: power-cut@every write/erase/swap-boundary, stale-approval/new-candidate, map-overlap, reject-fail, floor. LOCAL commit only → exact hive-codex re-pass. DO-NOT-FLASH + Roy tg_pk gate stand.
**★ APP-SEAM FLASHSINK SUB-INCREMENT SPEC (pickup-ready; GATED behind a clean re-review of 9135db2 — do NOT start until re-pass clean; supervisor sequencing).** Files = `rak4630-fw/platforms/rak4630/{src/ota.rs, src/main.rs, build.rs}`. Contract (core-blessed staging ruling + my OTA-META metadata-region choice + F1):
> (1) **ota.rs consume rak-geometry:** `SLOT_B_BASE`→`DFU_ORIGIN` (0x91000), `SLOT_SIZE`/`capacity()`→`ACTIVE_LEN` (0x6D000; matches the boot gate `payload_size≤ACTIVE_LEN` bound). (2) **★F1 app-half — FULL-SLOT ERASE:** `begin()` MUST erase the WHOLE DFU slot `DFU[0..DFU_LEN]` (not just payload-rounded), so the unauthenticated tail `DFU[payload_size..ACTIVE_LEN]` is 0xFF — ELSE the boot gate's tail-all-0xFF assert (9135db2) REJECTS a legit image. (3) **Receiver flow (#19/#35):** use `r2_update::OtaReceiver` (import the SIGNED one BY NAME — NOT the legacy unsigned `r2_hive_core::ota::OtaReceiver`): `new(ctx, PT_FIRMWARE_FULL, FlashSink)` → `push(&[u8])->Result<(RxProgress, consumed), RxError>` (preserve `sdu[consumed..]` post-package bytes) → `finish(self)->(AppliedUpdate, S, prefix:[u8;201])`. `abort()` idempotent + safe after a FAILED/partial `begin()`. (4) **commit_swap (ORDER = the core atomicity contract):** payload→DFU[0..] via FlashSink (verify-before-write) → finish → write `prefix[201]` (header137+sig64) → `OTA_META[0..201]` → set STATE `[0xF0;4]` SWAP_MAGIC **LAST** (plain Nvmc; embassy-boot magic word). Crash anywhere before the magic = no swap = old image boots (safe); corrupt after = boot-gate `verify_staged_slot` Err = fail-closed. (5) persona read `0x12000`→`PERSONA_ORIGIN` (0x22000). (6) app `build.rs` FLASH origin→`ACTIVE_ORIGIN` (0x24000) + VTOR reloc; reconcile parked stash `6dcfccc` (KEEP its embassy_boot relink@0x24000 + VTOR; DROP the obsolete 201→204 align — no approval record anymore). (7) then compile app+boot TOGETHER → exact hive-codex re-pass. DO-NOT-FLASH + Roy tg_pk gate stand.

**SUCCESSOR PROGRESS (local-only, no push):** ✅ increment 1 = `crates/rak-geometry` (d41657f) — shared map + KATs. ✅ increment 2 BOOTLOADER HALF = `ecad226`→**`9135db2` (F1-F4 re-pass fixes; rak4630-fw ahead 7, LOCAL; re-review pinned @9135db2)** — SUPERSEDES cad8b57's buggy gate. Bootloader rewritten: ALWAYS-VERIFY @progress==0 (NO approval-digest — supervisor Occam refutation, verified vs embassy-boot-0.7.0; progress==0 = proven pristine DFU) → kills C1(dead approval write)+H1(stale flag) by construction; C2 checked-reject (erase STATE→READBACK non-SWAP→erase DFU, else fail-stop sys_reset); C3 build.rs+runtime both consume rak-geometry (memory.x DFU end 0x100000→0xFF000, frees JOURNAL); H2 payload gate USES VerifiedUpdate (0<size≤ACTIVE_LEN, PT_FIRMWARE_FULL, vector sanity); C4/#6 floor read from JOURNAL (dev-explicit-0 when absent); H3/H4 PROD = compile_error! fail-closed (no prod path boots writable — pending ACL+prod-ctx+journal-writer), only `--features dev` compiles. Then compile app+boot together, exact hive-codex re-pass. **THEN prod hardening** (separate, coordinated + METAL): nRF52840 ACL(BOOTLOADER+PERSONA)+partition-wrap, real prod DeviceContext identity sources (device_id origin, class/carrier consts — provisioning-coordinated), JOURNAL pending/confirm WRITER (absent⇒fail-closed) — each flips a piece of the prod compile_error! off. **NEXT increments (the safety-critical gate state-machine — do FRESH, carefully):** (2) wire rak-geometry into the bootloader (replace local consts) + the gate = ALWAYS-VERIFY gated on embassy-boot's progress counter (supervisor Occam refutation 2026-07-13, VERIFIED vs embassy-boot-0.7.0 — the approval-digest record is DROPPED; see the CORRECTED-MAP req (2) above for the full rationale). Gate flow in bootloader main, BEFORE prepare_boot(): read STATE magic; if !=Swap → prepare_boot as normal (Boot/Revert/DfuDetach, zero crypto). If ==Swap → read current_progress() (STATE progress words): progress==0 (PRISTINE DFU, proven — first swap op touches only the scratch page) → read 137B header + 64B sig from OTA-META prefix + stream DFU payload → verify_staged_slot(header, sig, dfu_payload_chunks, ctx) → PASS → prepare_boot() (begins swap); FAIL → checked-reject (erase STATE→readback non-SWAP→erase DFU, else fail-stop). progress>0 (swap already begun, DFU scrambled) → NEVER verify, NEVER reject/erase → prepare_boot() (embassy resumes/reverts). No approval record, no digest, no candidate-binding — the durable authorized-signal IS the progress counter. KAT-pin the STATE layout (magic@0/valid@WRITE_SIZE/progress@2·WRITE_SIZE) + re-verify on embassy bump. (3) checked reject: erase STATE → READBACK proves non-SWAP → only THEN erase DFU; else fail-stop (no DFU erase). (4) payload gate (H2): 0<payload_size≤ACTIVE_LEN (not DFU_LEN — swap copies ACTIVE only), require PT_FIRMWARE_FULL, USE the returned VerifiedUpdate (check payload_type), bootable-vector sanity (ACTIVE[0..8] plausible SP+reset). (5) dev/prod DeviceContext split (H3): prod = real persona/board/device/battery from the sealed persona + board consts, fail-closed if unavailable; dev = explicit bench wildcard. (6) confirmed floor → the JOURNAL page (0xFF000, separate erasable, NOT the OTA-META candidate page); pending/confirm lifecycle writer; NO floor=0 fallback (absent journal ⇒ fail-closed, not 0). (7) app side: build.rs memory.x FROM rak-geometry; app persona read 0x12000→PERSONA_ORIGIN; ota.rs SLOT_B_BASE→DFU_ORIGIN, capacity→ACTIVE_LEN; commit_swap(prefix→OTA_META, SWAP magic LAST). (8) H4 BPROT/ACL — MANDATORY in increment 2 (coordinator correction: NOT a follow-up). PROD build applies reset-time BPROT/ACL (protect BOOTLOADER 0x0-0x20000 + PERSONA 0x22000-0x24000, partition-wrap app Nvmc writes); DEV/bench = the explicitly-named unprotected build; a prod build lacking protection FAILS at compile time (compile_error!). nRF52840 = ACL regions (not nRF52832 BPROT); the bootloader configures ACL before load(). (9) falsifier tests (progress-gate model — the substitution/stale-approval falsifiers are RETIRED with the digest; there is no skip-flag to attack): host KATs — (a) FRESH-TAMPER: State::Swap + progress==0 + a mutated DFU payload byte OR bad sig OR seq≤floor ⇒ verify_staged_slot FAILS ⇒ checked-reject (never boots); (b) RESUME-NEVER-REJECT: State::Swap + progress>0 ⇒ gate NEVER calls verify and NEVER erases/rejects (asserts prepare_boot resumes); (c) VERIFY-WINDOW POWER-CUT: crash between verify-pass and prepare_boot's first progress write ⇒ progress stays 0 ⇒ re-verify pristine DFU (idempotent, same verdict); (d) MID-SWAP POWER-CUT matrix: mock-flash crash at each swap/erase boundary ⇒ resume completes, never re-verifies scrambled DFU; (e) payload>ACTIVE_LEN reject, wrong payload_type reject; (f) STATE-layout KAT (progress-word offsets match embassy-boot); (g) the ELF alloc-free symbol gate. Then compile app+boot, LOCAL commit, exact hive-codex re-pass. cad8b57's buggy gate stays until increment 2 rewrites it.

## 🔨🚧 BUILDING — P3 USB-PAIR simple-secure PERIPHERAL SM (task #67) — supervisor GO 2026-07-12 against R2-PROVISION v0.50 @0f61c81
**★ GO #4 = BUILD ORDER (supervisor 2026-07-12):** build the simple pairing PERIPHERAL SM INTO the xiaobridge fw against twin-clean **v0.50 @`0f61c81`** (verified: ancestor of specs HEAD aff328a on spec-conformance-v0.2), regenerate vectors, re-verify terminal MACs, THEN reflash the XIAO so pairing lights over the live USB link (android runs PairingHost over ttyACM1 = the bench-critical reflash). BLE-beacon reflash stays DEFERRED behind WiFi; keep LoRa/USB bridge live; fold BLE into the same reflash if convenient. OK to install pyserial in a venv for a **DTR-LOW (no-reset) banner read** for hive_id/TG.
**✅ SPEC READ @0f61c81 (scratchpad/R2-PROVISION-0f61c81.md §5.3.4 lines 448-798).** Frame vocab (R2-USB §3.7 control `[0xFF]‖CBOR({0:msg_type,1:fields})`): 4 PAIR_HELLO_HOST host→p `{}` · 5 PAIR_COMMIT p→host `{1:commit(32)}` · 13 PAIR_HOST_REVEAL host→p `{1:eph_pk_host(32),2:nonce_host(32)}` · 6 PAIR_REVEAL p→host `{1:eph_pk_p(32),2:nonce_p(32)}` · 7 PAIR_CONFIRM host→p `{1:confirm_mac(16)}` · 8 PAIR_DONE p→host `{1:done_mac(16)}` · 14 PAIR_ACK host→p `{1:ack_mac(16)}` · 9 RECONNECT_CHALLENGE host→p `{1:nonce_rc(16)}` · 10 RECONNECT_RESPONSE p→host `{1:tag(16)}` · 11 PAIR_ABORT either `{1:reason tstr}`. (msg_type 12=observation, 15=retired.) **PERIPHERAL SM:** recv HELLO(4)→RETAIN persisted key, gen fresh eph+nonce, send COMMIT(5); recv HOST_REVEAL(13); send REVEAL(6); Z=X25519, reject all-zero→ABORT{bad_key}; recv CONFIRM(7) verify confirm-host MAC; send DONE(8); recv ACK(14) verify ack-host MAC→**PERSIST K**. Reconnect: recv CHALLENGE(9)→tag=HMAC(link_key,"r2-usb-reconnect-v1"‖nonce_rc‖usb_link_id)[..16]→RESPONSE(10); activation host-local (peripheral proves to host only). Idempotent in-session dup (RAM, 60s terminal timeout): dup CONFIRM→resend DONE, dup ACK→no-op. Key preservation: persisted key retained until final ACK-verify; re-pair on any doubt (no journal/gen/rotation/crash-recovery). transcript = eph_pk_host‖eph_pk_p‖nonce_host‖nonce_p (128B). usb_link_id = CAPS hive_id_bytes (16B) = HKDF("r2-usb-link-v1",device_master_secret,"")[..16].
**✅ TERMINAL MACs RE-VERIFIED byte-exact vs v0.50 (supervisor's re-verify check DONE):** usb_pair.rs labels + asserted hex == spec UP14/UP18 (confirm `4e4c5ff2…`/done `08ba274f…`/ack `1ec03c3d…`/reconnect `2f62edaa…`); KDF domains did NOT move (spec line 570: byte-exact constructions unchanged, naming-only). 14 usb_pair tests green. Crypto restored @5fc3a20 is spec-valid — no revector needed.
**⚠ SCOPE BOUND (spec §5.3.4 lines 456-460, 573-602):** pairing establishes `link_key` ONLY. Key-bearing USB-SAS join (§3 JoinInvite/JoinResponse group-key install) is SPEC-GATED **fail-closed** until the owed `JoinInvite`↔`link_key` invite-MAC binding lands — do NOT implement join key install; the SM ends at link_key + reconnect.
**✅ BUILT + BYTE-PROVEN (2026-07-12) — reflash PENDING android integration contract + supervisor ping.**
**dfr1195-fw commits:** 238a6de (crate) + b54915b (fw wiring). **NEW crate `dfr1195-fw/crates/r2-usb-pair`**
(host-testable no_std lib, root-ws member, xtensa-buildable via fw path-dep): crypto + §3.7 control-frame
codec + peripheral SM. **11 host KATs GREEN incl. the refutation-grade ones:** full choreography emits
UP14.sequence `frame_hex` BYTE-EXACT (HELLO→COMMIT→HOST_REVEAL→REVEAL→CONFIRM→DONE→ACK), reconnect ==

FIX (agreed, fail-CLOSED): NVS ops return Result + refuse-to-START an OTA if the floor is unreadable + durably stage {seq,payload_hash} BEFORE esp_ota set_boot + reconcile pending after mark-valid (same discipline as the RAK FlashSink).

## 🧩 WASM HOST — LINKABLE BASE (NEW workstream, Roy GO 2026-07-10, task #64; parallel to RAK)
Roy ruled BUILD the linkable base; hive owns the **wasm HOST** (base HOSTS wasm ensemble modules = Level 2, greenfield — NOT r2-hive-wasm, which is R2 compiled TO wasm). Ref: r2-specifications docs/proposals/R2-LINKABLE-BASE-AND-VARIANT-MANAGEMENT-2026-07-10.md (D.3 steps 4-5). **Prep design committed: docs/WASM-HOST-LINKABLE-BASE-PREP.md (c709e23).**
- **Two ABI surfaces** (both = the §12.4 Plugin trait lowered to repr(C) per proposal A.5.3): module-EXPORTS (execute/init/poll → wasm ptr+len) + host-IMPORTS (the capabilities.requires §12.3 syscall surface = "the host-import surface"). A wasm module becomes a Rust Plugin impl trampolining into its exports → plugs into existing engine dispatch.
- **Phasing (D.3 4-5, core A.5 binding):** std host (wasmtime) + browser (native WebAssembly) FIRST; then esp32s3+PSRAM wasm3; **nrf52840 = ONE bounded (<=32KB) boot-reserved wasm3 slot only** (A.5.1 — general multi-module REFUTED; binding constraint = 64KB-page CONTIGUITY on MMU-less heap, not total RAM). **Level-0 hot-path/crypto NEVER modularized** (A.5.4 — route/dedup/wire/CBOR/FNV, radio io_task, HMAC/HKDF/Ed25519). Host = orchestration-class only.
- **✅ M1 LANDED — gate LIFTED.** R2-PLUGIN v0.6 §12.4.3 Frozen ABI RATIFIED (specs 73af517, in my local checkout; read fully). Froze: AbiResponse[128]/AbiError[64]/AbiResult (repr(C,u8)); PluginVTableV1 (repr(C), abi_version FIRST, id, execute/init/poll/name extern C, inst=*mut c_void); ONE export `__r2_plugin_vtable_v1`; init/poll required (r2-forge no-op); abi_hash = SHA-256 over canonical schema, load gate order = verify sig → abi_hash EXACT-match → instantiate. 4 rulings: 8B abi_hash trunc in UpdateHeader / exact-match v1 / one-vtable-per-module / init-poll-required-noop. core implements the repr(C) types + r2-forge shim-gen + vtable KAT.

Monolithic images = all-zero.

- **🔴 INTEROP BLOCKER + RESOLUTION (core 5447034: r2-forge L2 wasm-emit UP, verified on real wasm32).** core built a real r2-forge module and found: Rust `#[no_mangle] pub static i32` lowers to a wasm GLOBAL holding the linear-memory ADDRESS of the value, NOT the value (e.g. __r2_abi_version global = 1048612, value 1 lives at that offset). My host reads globals as VALUES (get_global i32) → would read 1048612 not 1 → interop FAILS. **CO-PIN DECISION (agreed w/ core): switch __r2_abi_version + __r2_plugin_id from GLOBALS → VALUE-RETURNING FUNCS** (`__r2_abi_version()->i32`, `__r2_plugin_id()->i32`): unambiguous cross-language (deref-address is a Rust-lowering leak a hand-WAT/non-Rust conformer wouldn't satisfy), cleanly Rust-emittable, consistent with __r2_abi_hash already a func (→ all metadata reads funcs, only `memory` non-func). Deviates from ratified 'global' → **route to specs as a §12.4.3.1 AMENDMENT (co-pinned w/ core).** FUNC exports + the 136B LE padding-zero AbiResult image are byte-locked (core confirmed on wasm32) — no change there; core supplies the AbiResult image KAT as the shared vector. **SPEC-FIRST HOLD: keep host at ratified global-read until specs amends, then flip get_global→get_typed_func (trivial) + update the conformance WAT (globals→funcs) → interop with core's real .wasm + KAT.**
